2. The operation of the special jury system does not deprive defendant of due process.

 

2220 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grossman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Kings County


45 Misc. 2d 557; 257 N.Y.S.2d 266; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2224



February 28, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions are in all respects granted as indicated herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who had been indicted for larceny of jewelry by false pretenses and possession of weapons, filed motions to suppress evidence pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 813-c, urging that the authorities gathered the evidence that supported the indictments through illegal wiretapping.


OVERVIEW: The authorities believed that one defendant was involved in the larceny of jewelry, and pursuant to § 813-a obtained an order authorizing the installation of an eavesdropping device in that defendant's service station, broke into the station, and installed a "bug." Conversations disclosed an unrelated crime involving additional defendants, who were arrested for weapons possession and indicted. The case went before the court on defendants' motions to suppress, which the court granted. The court held that a court order issued under § 813-a could not serve as a "search warrant" under the Warrant Clause of the Fourth Amendment to validate an intrusion or invasion into a constitutionally protected area. A "search warrant" may not constitutionally authorize a search for or seizure of mere evidence in the nature of conversations or verbal statements. Only such eavesdropping that violated the Fourth Amendment was determined to be unconstitutional. The Fourth Amendment was violated when the eavesdropping was effectuated (1) by means of a physical invasion or intrusion, (2) upon a constitutionally protected area. Defendant's service station was such a constitutionally protected area.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motions to suppress evidence in the action against them for larceny of jewelry and possession of weapons.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- electronic eavesdropping -- ex parte order authorizing electronic eavesdropping (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-a) cannot constitutionally be used as warrant to intrude upon person's business premises and search for and seize conversations (U. S. Const., 4th and 5th Amdts.); nor can such inadmissible conversations constitute probable cause for issuance of search warrant pursuant to which pistols were seized as physical evidence (Code Crim. Pro., § 792); such conversations and such physical evidence are ordered suppressed (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-c); since there was no other evidence before Grand Jury, indictment is ordered dismissed -- United States Supreme Court decisions govern -- to extent to which sections 792 and 813-a of Code of Criminal Procedure authorize seizure of "property constituting evidence of crime" and of conversations as "evidence of crime" only, they violate Fourth, Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments -- court has power to hold pretrial hearing and order suppression of unconstitutionally seized evidence; thus, District Attorney has right of appeal which he would not have if court made  [***2] these rulings at trial.

1. The United States Constitution (4th Amdt.) provides that "The right of the people to be secure in their persons, houses, papers, and effects, against unreasonable searches and seizures, shall not be violated, and no Warrants shall issue, but upon probable cause". A person's place of business is such a constitutionally protected area. The police may obtain an ex parte order (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-a) authorizing them to install an electronic eavesdropping device; but when, in order to install and conceal such a device, they break and enter or physically intrude or trespass on constitutionally protected premises, they have made an unreasonable, unlawful and unconstitutional search. Any evidence thus obtained is inadmissible and should be suppressed (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-c). When the police obtain a search warrant (Code Crim. Pro., § 792) based upon such inadmissible evidence, no probable cause is established for the issuance of the warrant, and hence the physical evidence which is seized pursuant to such a warrant must likewise be suppressed (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-c). Furthermore, if a Grand Jury has issued an indictment based solely on such [***3] inadmissible evidence, both physical and intangible, the indictment should be dismissed.

2. The New York State Constitution (art. I, § 12) contains the same provision as does the Federal Fourth Amendment. However, the constitutional principle which excludes unlawfully seized evidence is commanded upon the States by the Federal Fourth Amendment via the Fourteenth Amendment. Therefore, the Federal standards stated by the decisions of the United States Supreme Court should determine the constitutionality of State legislation which authorizes eavesdropping or wire tapping, such as section 813-a of our Code of Criminal Procedure, which provides that "An ex parte order for eavesdropping" -- which is otherwise prohibited by the Penal Law ( § 738) -- "may be issued * * * upon oath or affirmation * * * that there is reasonable ground to believe that evidence of crime may be thus obtained".

3. A grand larceny of jewelry by false pretenses having been committed, the police made affidavit showing that there was reasonable ground to believe that one Scandifia was implicated in that crime, and obtained an ex parte order authorizing them to install an electronic eavesdropping device (Code Crim.  [***4] Pro., § 813-a) in a service station owned by Scandifia. They installed the device by breaking and illegally entering the service station in the early morning hours. At two-month intervals they obtained orders extending the original order's duration (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-a; cf. Code Crim. Pro., § 802). Meantime, they obtained a similar ex parte order authorizing electronic eavesdropping of the business premises of one Ferrara; and there too they surreptitiously installed a device by physically intruding upon Ferrara's constitutionally protected premises. This order was based on an affidavit alleging conspiracy and coercion and "shylocking", but not showing probable cause. By means of these electronic devices, the police listened to all conversations, not only telephonic ones. Apparently they heard nothing relating to those crimes. What they eventually did hear, on the Scandifia eavesdrop device, were conversations between Scandifia and one Grossman indicating their unlawful possession of two pistols and bullets and a conspiracy among those two and Ferrara and one Pistone to assault or kill any and all stool pigeons. A police officer presented an affidavit as to these inadmissible [***5] conversations and obtained a warrant to search an automobile owned by Grossman (Code Crim. Pro., § 792). The warrant was executed and disclosed two pistols. On motions of defendants and after a hearing thereon, the seized pistols and the overheard conversations are ordered suppressed (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-c); and, since there was no other evidence before the Grand Jury, the indictment which charges all of the defendants with conspiracy to commit assault or murder and which further charges defendants Grossman and Scandifia with illegal possession of weapons, is dismissed.

4. Ex parte orders authorizing eavesdropping (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-a) cannot be used as "Warrants", under the Fourth Amendment of the United Statse Constitution, so as to authorize a physical intrusion or invasion into constitutionally protected premises in order to search for and seize evidence consisting of verbal statements or conversations.

5. Furthermore, the overheard conversations concerned, not a jewelry larceny as set forth in the supporting affidavit, but pistols and bullets and a conspiracy to assault or kill any and all stool pigeons. It cannot be said that, as to such unrelated crimes, the [***6] eavesdropping order or the extensions of that order were based on "reasonable ground" (Code Crim. Pro., § 813-a) or "probable cause" (U. S. Const., 4th Amdt.).

6. Moreover, the United States Constitution (4th Amdt.) prohibits any search warrants except those "particularly describing the * * * things to be seized." The things to be seized in this case were conversations evidencing particular crimes; yet the order necessarily authorized electronic listening to "any and all conversations, communications and discussions". It seems that no electronic listening or recording device has yet been invented which will shut itself off when a privileged or merely social conversation begins.

7. Section 792 of the Code of Criminal Procedure authorizes search warrants for the seizure not only of (a) the fruits of a crime and (b) instrumentalities used in committing a crime and (c) contraband unlawfully possessed, but (d) "property constituting evidence of crime"; and section 813-a of the Code of Criminal Procedure authorizes orders for overhearing and recording conversations from which "evidence of crime" may be obtained. To the extent that the quoted words may be taken to authorize the search [***7] and seizure of tangible property on the sole ground that it is evidence of guilt, and of intangibles which are mere conversations or verbal statements, said sections 792 and 813-a violate constitutional protections against privacy and self incrimination (U. S. Const., 4th and 5th Amdts.), and perhaps also the protection which due process of law affords (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.) against involuntary confessions.

8. The court has power under sections 813-c, 813-d, and 813-e of the Code of Criminal Procedure, and under its inherent powers as well, to entertain a pretrial motion and hold a hearing and suppress intangible evidence which has been unconstitutionally seized under cover of an order made under section 813-a of the Code of Criminal Procedure. By adopting this pretrial procedure, the court affords the District Attorney a right of appeal which he would not have if the court were to make these rulings at the trial.

 

2221 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Paduano v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


45 Misc. 2d 718; 257 N.Y.S.2d 531; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2268



February 15, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the reasons above noted, the plaintiffs' motion for temporary injunction is denied, and defendants' cross motion to dismiss the complaint is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought a permanent injunction against defendant city's implementation of New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 141.08, which provided for the fluoridation of the city's water supply. The city sought dismissal of the taxpayers' complaint, which alleged that the city could not legally expend the funds for § 141.08 because it violated the Fourteenth Amendment, N.Y. Const. art. I, § 1, and the New York City Public Health Law.


OVERVIEW: The purpose of New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 141.08 was to prevent tooth decay in children. The court held that the New York City Department of Health was empowered by New York City, N.Y., Charter §§ 555 - 558 to enact statutes for the furtherance and protection of human health. Section 141.08 offended no state public policy, contravened no state statute or municipal ordinance, and was not in excess of the Department's power. Section 141.08 did not violate New York City, N.Y., Charter § 225 because the city was not issuing bonds for the financing of the fluoridation. The city was not required to prove that fluoridation of the water supply was the most efficacious manner of distribution of the fluoride to children. Fluoridation did not breach the Equal Protection Clause by discrimination in favor of children because the children would be adults one day. The health of children was a legitimate area of public and governmental concern and New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 141.08 was an appropriate exercise of the city's police power. The court relied on other case law regarding fluoridation statutes in its dismissal of the taxpayers' action.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayers' motion for a temporary injunction and granted the city's cross motion to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- fluoridation of water -- in action to enjoin New York City's proposed water fluoridation program, complaint is dismissed -- fluoridation is health problem within jurisdiction of Board of Health -- such board's enactment of section 141.08 of New York City Health Code, authorizing program, is valid -- expenditure of funds from expense budget for such program is valid -- issue of impairment of religious freedom of group by program not considered since not raised in complaint -- means here used to provide fluorides by adding fluorides to water is valid -- fluoridation not discriminatory in favor of children -- no rights of citizens invaded by fluoridation -- courts will not interfere with establishment of fluoridation program; question is for legislative and executive branches of government.

1. In an action to enjoin the proposed program for the fluoridation of the municipal water supply of New York City as authorized by section 141.08 of the New York City Health Code enacted by the Board of Health,  [***2] plaintiffs' motion for a temporary injunction is denied and defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint is granted.

2. Regardless of its validity, the fluoridation program is directed towards the security of life and health of the citizens of New York City and towards coping with the public health problem of tooth decay and dental neglect, particularly among children. Even though there is a strong difference of opinion as to its value, the problem is one of health and is within the jurisdiction of the Department of Health.

3. Section 141.08 of the Health Code is not against public policy, contravenes no State statute or municipal ordinance and is not in excess of the Health Department's power. A cause of action wherein plaintiffs allege that the city may not lawfully expend funds for the proposed project because no local law has been passed authorizing such action is dismissed.

4. The expenditure of funds from the expense budget for the acquisition and installation of the necessary equipment and facilities is proper. A project need not be handled through the capital budget and capital budget appropriation if it is intended that the costs of the project be met wholly out of the [***3] expense budget appropriation and not by any city borrowing. While allowance of capital expenditures through the device of inclusion in the expense budget may afford a method of circumvention of the procedures surrounding capital budget appropriations, this procedure is legally permissible and there is no basis presented for judicial interference.

5. Since there is no allegation in the complaint that the religious freedom of certain groups in the community will be unconstitutionally impaired by fluoridation, the issue cannot be considered.

6. The existence of other methods by which fluorides may be provided is irrelevant. The means used here of adding it to the water supply is lawful.

7. Fluoridation does not discriminate because only children benefit. Children become adults and fluoridation will ultimately affect all. The health of children is a legitimate area of public and governmental concern, whether under the police power of the State or in the exercise of the State's power to protect the general welfare.

8. Fluoridation does not unconstitutionally invade the rights of citizens.

9. Until scientific evidence as to harmful effects of fluoridation exceeds the speculation,  [***4] now existing, courts will not interfere and the controversy should remain with the legislative and executive branches of government.

 

2222 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Caminito v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


45 Misc. 2d 241; 256 N.Y.S.2d 670; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2278



February 10, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff criminal defendant filed an action against defendant city, alleging false arrest and imprisonment, malicious prosecution, and conspiracy arising from his detention at a police station and extended interrogation without the ability to communicate with his family, friends, or attorney. The interrogation resulted in a confession, and criminal defendant was convicted. Criminal defendant filed a summary judgment motion.


OVERVIEW: A victim was shot during a holdup, but described assailants before his death. This information and other leads brought police to criminal defendant, who was brought in for questioning. After 27 hours of withheld contact from his family, friends, and attorney, criminal defendant confessed. He was then arrested and convicted solely on the basis of his confession. However, criminal defendant's conviction was vacated because of constitutional infirmities in the questioning and arrest of criminal defendant. Criminal's complaint alleged false arrest and imprisonment, malicious prosecution, and conspiracy, upon which he filed a summary judgment motion. Because of the manner of the investigation, questioning, and detention, the police lacked probable cause to believe that criminal defendant had committed a felony. Thus, city had no right to detain or arrest criminal defendant. Despite this, the court allowed the false arrest claim to go to the jury. The court also held that the false imprisonment claim did not sufficiently state a cause of action and that the issue of whether "malice" occurred to prove malicious prosecution was a question for the jury.


OUTCOME: The court denied criminal defendant's summary judgment motion, dismissed certain causes of action, and issued conclusions of law as to other causes of action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] False imprisonment -- lack of probable cause -- in action for false imprisonment and malicious prosecution, where no issue of fact exists, issue of probable cause may be determined by court as question of law -- police officer lacked probable cause to believe that plaintiff committed murder -- even if probable cause existed, plaintiff's arrest was unlawful ab initio; plaintiff granted summary judgment in action for false imprisonment but damages will be determined by triers of fact -- defendant prevented plaintiff from complying with statutes dealing with notice of claim -- moreover, notice of claim is timely where filed after indictment dismissed in 1963; issue of timeliness left to trial court -- plaintiff not entitled to recovery for imprisonment after judgment of conviction -- presumption of probable cause was overcome by use of void confession against plaintiff -- question of malice in action for malicious prosecution is left to jury -- cause of action for conspiracy adds nothing to primary torts alleged.

1. In an action to recover damages for false arrest and imprisonment and for malicious prosecution, where there is no dispute as to the facts, and no conflicting inferences [***2] may fairly be drawn from the circumstances, the issue of probable cause may be disposed of by the court as a question of law.

2. The undisputed facts show no circumstances which warranted the apprehension, detention and arrest of plaintiff in 1941. Nowhere does it appear that plaintiff, and two others, resembled the persons described by a murder victim to a police officer before the victim's death, or that the victim did or could see the getaway car and its driver parked, according to a witness for the Grand Jury, some 10 feet in front of the victim's car at a time when darkness had set in. Accordingly, the police officer, as a matter of law, lacked probable cause to believe that plaintiff had committed a felony and therefore had no right to arrest plaintiff.

3. Even assuming that probable cause existed, the violation by defendant's officers of section 165 of the Code of Criminal Procedure by failing to take plaintiff before a Magistrate for arraignment without unnecessary delay, rendered the arrest unlawful ab initio and it continued to be unlawful until plaintiff was lawfully committed pursuant to a warrant. While plaintiff was arraigned shortly after he was formally arrested [***3] and booked, his detention in the precinct house for more than 33 hours prior to the formal arrest constituted an unlawful detention. Detention in a police station constitutes an arrest. Plaintiff was in fact under arrest for all of the time he was interrogated and subjected to the coercion applied to compel his confession. This arrest and detention became unlawful ab initio and plaintiff is entitled to damages from the commencement of his detention until the time of his arraignment 40 hours later. Plaintiff is entitled to summary judgment on the first cause of action but, since the damages sustained for the 40-hour period are relatively minimal compared to the 22-year period involved, an assessment of such damages should not be had but it should be determined by the triers of the facts of the remaining issues.

4. Plaintiff's noncompliance with the statutory provisions relative to the service of a notice of claim and the commencement of the action was caused by defendant's conduct in unlawfully placing plaintiff under restraint and therefore defendant cannot complain of plaintiff's failure to file a notice of claim.

5. Moreover, a cause of action for false imprisonment does [***4] not accrue until the party has been discharged from restraint. The indictment against plaintiff was not dismissed until 1963. Therefore the provisions of the statute were complied with. Since, however, there may be an arguable question of law that the false imprisonment was complete when the arraignment took place, and that the cause of action accrued at that time, the issue is referred to the trial court for determination.

6. As a matter of law, plaintiff is not entitled to any recovery for the imprisonment subsequent to the judgment of conviction. Such detention pursuant to a judgment, regular on its face, is not actionable even if the judgment is thereafter set aside.

7. Any presumption of probable cause relating to the prosecution was overcome as a matter of law by proof that defendant's employees caused to be exhibited to the Grand Jury and the trial jury the void confession which was the sole proximate cause of plaintiff's indictment and conviction.

8. As to the cause of action for malicious prosecution, malice may be inferred by the trier of the facts from the circumstance that there was a lack of probable cause for the institution of the criminal proceedings, but such [***5] inference may not be drawn by the court, nor can the trial court direct a jury to draw such an inference. The jury may presume malice but it is not required to do so.

9. A third cause of action charging a conspiracy adds nothing substantively to the primary torts alleged. In a civil action for conspiracy, the tort is the illicit acts and not the agreement.

 

2223 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mt. Vernon v. East Hudson Parkway Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


45 Misc. 2d 471; 257 N.Y.S.2d 51; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2281



February 10, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Mount Vernon sought to enjoin defendant East Hudson Parkway Authority (authority) from appropriating certain property belonging to the city and others for the purpose of widening a roadway. Prior to service of its answer, the authority filed a motion to dismiss, alleging lack of personal and subject matter jurisdiction, lack of the city's capacity to sue, and failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 457, the authority allocated funds for the acquisition of the city's property and the expansion of a state parkway. The city sought to enjoin the act, and the authority entered a motion to dismiss. Under N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3211(c), the court treated the motion like a summary judgment motion and considered the parties' supporting affidavits. The court granted the motion and dismissed the case. The court held that the authority was empowered, under N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 457(4), to acquire property in the way it did, and that the statute enjoyed a presumption of constitutionality that the city's pleadings, which attacked its reasonableness, could not overcome. The court held that the question of necessity in eminent domain cases was within the legislative discretion and not a proper subject for judicial review.


OUTCOME: After considering supporting affidavits, the court granted the authority's motion to dismiss because the city's complaint was legally insufficient.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- East Hudson Parkway Authority -- although consent of municipality is required if East Hudson Parkway Authority appropriates municipality's street or property (Public Authorities Law, § 457, subd. 3), no such consent is needed if State Superintendent of Public Works makes such appropriation for said Authority (Public Authorities Law, § 457, subd. 4) -- whether eight-lane widening will not be needed until year 1985, and whether six-lane widening would be enough and would not interfere with city's urban renewal plans, are matters within power and discretion of appropriating authorities, not courts -- city's complaint dismissed.

1. The East Hudson Parkway Authority was created in 1960 (Public Authorities Law, § 450 et seq.), to operate and reconstruct the Westchester County parkway system, which includes the Cross County Parkway. At first, its power of condemnation was subject to the proviso that it could not condemn property of a municipality without such municipality's consent (Public Authorities Law, § 457, subd. 3). However, the Legislature amended this section by adding a subdivision 4 in 1962 and by amending said subdivision 4 further in 1963,  [***2] so as to provide a simpler and more expeditious procedure whereby the State Superintendent of Public Works, when requested by the Authority, may appropriate property for it by the procedure used under the Highway Law ( § 30). There are similar procedures for the Thruway and for interstate routes and for others (e.g., Public Authorities Law, §§ 358, 529, 1007; Highway Law, § 340-b). The procedure under subdivision 4 of section 457 of the Public Authorities Law is obviously an alternative to that under subdivision 3 and eliminates any need for municipal consent. Subdivision 4 is constitutional and valid.

2. The City of Mount Vernon sues to enjoin and restrain an appropriation which will widen, from four lanes to eight lanes, five miles of the Cross County Parkway, of which one mile lies in said city. The city urges that six lanes would be enough and would eliminate the need to appropriate a certain city street and certain private property, that the eight-lane taking will interfere with the city's master plan for urban renewal, and that there is no need for an eight-lane highway except as projected into the year 1985. However, all of those matters are within the discretion and [***3] powers of the appropriating authorities, not the courts.

3. The affidavits for the defendants -- the Authority and the Superintendent of Public Works -- show that the requisites for the appropriation under the statutes (Public Authorities Law, § 457, subd. 4; Highway Law, § 30) have been complied with. On a motion to dismiss a complaint for legal insufficiency, affidavits may be considered ( CPLR 3211, subd. [c]). Defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint for legal insufficiency is granted.

 

2224 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Binghamton v. Gillett


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Broome County


46 Misc. 2d 48; 259 N.Y.S.2d 359; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2284



February 9, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town filed a motion for summary judgment in its action against defendant property owners. The town sought to enjoin the owners from maintaining and/or occupying a trailer on their land in violation of its ordinance that required a building permit or a certificate of occupancy. Further, the owners' land was not zoned for the erection or occupancy of trailers.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that the town's zoning ordinances were unconstitutional, usurious in nature, and contrary to their property rights. The owners also claimed that the structure was permanently placed upon a permanent foundation and therefore was not a trailer. The court found that the owners could not challenge the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance because there was no evidence that they applied for and were denied an building permit by the town's zoning board. Because they were challenging the ordinance's constitutionality as it applied to them, it was incumbent that they comply with the provisions of the ordinance before attacking its validity. Further, N.Y., Town Zoning Ordinance§ 905 gave the town the authority to institute the appropriate action to prevent the unlawful construction of a building or to prevent any illegal act on the premises. Even if the structure on the owners' property was not a trailer, they were still required to obtain a building permit. The court granted the town's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to the town but stayed the injunctive relief for a period of 30 days in order to give the owners time to apply for the appropriate permits from the town. If the owners failed to apply for the permits, they would be enjoined from maintaining and occupying the trailer on their land.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- certification of Zoning Ordinance by Town Clerk is presumptive evidence of adoption thereof -- in action to enjoin defendants from maintaining trailer, defendants cannot question constitutionality of ordinance as applied to their land until they have applied for, and been denied, permit -- since defendants deny that their structure is trailer, they must obtain building permit under Zoning Ordinance; if it is trailer, they must comply with provisions of Zoning Ordinance pertaining to trailers; plaintiff granted injunction.

1. The certification by a Town Clerk that a Zoning Ordinance was duly passed is presumptive evidence of adoption, publication and posting, and must be taken as established in the absence of a question of fact raised by defendants as to its proper passage.

2. In an action to enjoin defendants from maintaining a trailer on their land on the ground that they did not obtain a building permit as required by the Zoning Ordinance and on the further ground that a trailer may not be erected or used on land in defendants' district, defenses concerning the constitutionality of the ordinances may not be considered until defendants [***2] have applied for and been denied a permit. Until then they cannot claim unconstitutionality as applied to their property.

3. Since defendants deny that their structure is a trailer, they must comply with the Zoning Ordinance by obtaining a permit. If it is a trailer, they have failed to comply with the provisions of the Zoning Ordinance respecting trailers. Plaintiff is entitled to summary judgment but the injunction will be stayed for a time during which defendants may apply for the appropriate permits.

 

2225 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Du Pell v. Hostetter


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


45 Misc. 2d 313; 256 N.Y.S.2d 980; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2306



February 2, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retailers brought an action for a declaratory judgment against defendant, the State Liquor Authority, testing the constitutionality of certain provisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 101-b, subd. 3. The retailers also sought a preliminary injunction restraining the Authority from enforcing the challenged sections of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the retailers were licensed to operate retail package stores at locations within and without the state. The court further found that the challenged sections involved the Authority's right to set a price schedule to which sellers, manufacturers, and wholesalers were required to comply. The court noted that the constitutionality of some of the sections had previously been upheld and, therefore, the court disposed of those allegations of the complaint. As to the other sections, the court held that the price-fixing mandated by the act was a proper exercise of the police power. The court reasoned that legislation concerning sales of goods, and incidentally affecting prices, had repeatedly been held valid. With respect to the preliminary injunction, the court concluded that the retailers failed to show that they had sustained, or would have sustained in the future, damage to a pecuniary interest. Accordingly, the court held that they were not aggrieved parties.


OUTCOME: The court denied the retailers' application for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Intoxicating liquors -- retail liquor prices -- provision of amendment to Alcoholic Beverage Control Law effected by chapter 531 of Laws of 1964 dealing with retail prices is constitutional -- plaintiffs have failed to overcome presumption of constitutionality of other provisions -- Bulletin No. 390 and rule 17 not unconstitutional -- plaintiffs, retailers, are not aggrieved persons as to section 9 of chapter 531 providing for wholesale pricing of liquor -- application for temporary injunction is denied.

1. Plaintiffs have failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality attaching to section 7 of chapter 531 of the Laws of 1964, which amended the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law so as to forbid the sale of brand liquors and wines to retailers except at prices shown on schedules filed by the sellers. Price-fixing is a proper exercise of the police power.

2. Plaintiffs, retailers, have also failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality attaching to section 10 of chapter 531 and section 11 of chapter 531. The repeal effected by section 11 was a necessary corollary to the enactment of the new price-fixing provisions of section 7 in relation to retailers.

3. The [***2] claim that Bulletin No. 390 of defendant Authority and the amended rule 17 were invalid resting on a charge that sections 13 and 14 of chapter 531 were void, falls since such sections were upheld as constitutional by Martin v. State Liq. Auth. (43 Misc 2d 682, affd. 15 N Y 2d 707).

4. Section 9 of chapter 531 amends the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law so as to require the filing of affirmations by the owners and agents of owners of brand liquor, and any wholesaler and anyone else filing a schedule, that the scheduled prices to wholesalers and retailers are "no higher than the lowest price at which such item of liquor was sold by such brand owner or such wholesaler designated as agent, or any related person, to any" wholesaler or retailer anywhere in any other State at any time during the month preceding the month the schedule is filed. Plaintiffs have failed to establish such an interest as to give them the right to challenge section 9. So far as plaintiffs are concerned, section 9 is not related to section 7 except in the possibility that the effect of section 9 might result in lower schedule prices to retailers. This is not damaging to plaintiffs and, therefore, they are [***3] not aggrieved parties.

5. The application for a temporary injunction is denied.

In re Estate of Commendatore


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Erie County


44 Misc. 2d 1079; 255 N.Y.S.2d 957; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2312



February 1, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a county commissioner of social welfare, commenced a proceeding to compel respondent executors to render and settle their accounts and to show cause why the commissioner's claim under N.Y. Soc. Welf. Act § 104 should not be paid. The matter came before the court on the executor's objections to the claim and to the constitutionality of the statutes relating to social welfare claims.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's grandchildren received public assistance. Upon the decedent's death, the commissioner sought to recover payment for the public assistance from the decedent's estate pursuant to § 104. The executors rejected the claim and claimed that the statutes allowing for such a procedure were unconstitutional. The court denied the constitutional challenge, concluding that the statutes did not deprive any distributee of the estate of property without due process of the law because the distributees had no legal title to the decedent's property during her lifetime. The court also determined that the commissioner was not required to exhaust his remedies against the relatives in any particular order as a prerequisite to recovery under § 104.


OUTCOME: The court rejected the executors' constitutional challenge and set the matter for a hearing.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Paupers -- liability of relatives of recipients of public assistance -- executor of grandmother of recipients of public assistance must settle claim of County Commissioner of Social Welfare (Social Welfare Law, §§ 101, 104); such claim is valid even as to sums paid to said grandchildren prior to 1963 amendment which codified decisions holding that liability of another relative is immaterial.

The executor of a grandmother of persons who received public assistance must render an accounting and settle the claim of the County Commissioner of Social Welfare for the sums advanced to said grandchildren of said decedent (Social Welfare Law, §§ 101, 104). The cited sections are of long standing and are constitutional. Section 104 was amended in 1963 to state that it is immaterial that another relative is also liable; but this amendment merely codified existing decisions which interpeted the statute to that same effect; hence the statute validly covers public assistance which was rendered prior to 1963.

 

2227 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


45 Misc. 2d 52; 256 N.Y.S.2d 205; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2330



January 26, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 1943, defendant filed a motion for resentencing of a sentence he received as a third offender for attempted grand larceny.


OVERVIEW: In 1951, defendant pleaded guilty to attempted grand larceny. Initially, he was sentenced to 5 to 10 years' imprisonment. In a subsequent habeas corpus proceeding, his conviction was vacated. On remand in 1954, he was again convicted on his guilty plea and sentenced as a second felony offender to a term of two and half to seven and half years imprisonment. In 1956, he was sentenced to 5 to 10 years' imprisonment as a second offender, when the court elected not to conduct a trial upon the issue of his identity as the same person convicted in 1951 and to treat him as a second offender upon the basis of an Indiana conviction, which he admitted. Upon resentence in 1960 as a third offender, defendant received the same sentence after admitting his identity as the person convicted in 1951. Defendant attacked the 1954 conviction, which was used as a predicate for the 1960 sentence. The court found that the amendment to § 1943 made by 1964 N.Y. Laws ch. 446 did not apply to predicate judgments of conviction had in New York State courts. The court held that relief by way of a motion for resentence was not available where the challenged predicate conviction was obtained in a New York court.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for resentence without prejudice to an application to vacate the judgment of conviction alleged to be invalid.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- multiple offender punishment -- 1964 amendment of section 1943 of Penal Law provides no remedy to defendant to challenge previous New York conviction, used for multiple offender punishment; to challenge constitutionality of prior conviction, defendant's remedy is writ of error coram nobis in trial court; motion for resentence denied.

Section 1943 of the Penal Law, as amended by chapter 446 of the Laws of 1964, permits challenge at the time of sentence to previous convictions relied upon to increase the allowable punishment where it is claimed that such convictions had been obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional rights. The remedy is by an objection at the time of sentence, the court to determine the merits of the objection and failure to challenge at the time of sentence is declared a waiver unless good cause be shown for such failure. Such amendment and the procedure therein do not apply to previous judgments of conviction, used as basis for multiple offender punishment, where the judgments were had in New York State, but do apply to out-of-State judgments. Accordingly, defendant's motion for resentence on the claim that a 1954 New York conviction [***2] could not be used as a predicate for third felony offender punishment is denied as not available. Defendant's remedy is to move to vacate the judgment in the trial court by a writ of error coram nobis.

State Nat'l Bank v. Laura


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Westchester County


45 Misc. 2d 430; 256 N.Y.S.2d 1004; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2339



January 23, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to dismiss is, therefore, in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor filed a motion for an order dismissing plaintiff bank's complaint on the ground that the bank did not have legal capacity to bring this action.


OVERVIEW: The bank filed suit against the debtor, who had possession of an automobile that the bank had financed, after the debtor had gone into default on the payments. The debtor filed a motion to dismiss on grounds that the bank did not have legal capacity to sue since it did not have a certificate to do business in New York. The court denied the motion. The court held that N.Y. Gen. Corp. Law §§ 210 and 218, by their express provisions, were not applicable to the bank, a national banking association, because the bank was a "moneyed corporation" and that since the bank was brought into existence under federal legislation, it did not come within New York's statutory requirements limiting the right of foreign corporations to sue.


OUTCOME: The court denied the debtor's motion to dismiss the bank's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Banks and banking -- capacity of national bank to sue -- foreign national bank, as moneyed corporation, does not require certificate of authority to do business as condition to bringing action in State courts -- national bank is exempt from requirements of State statutes -- attorney's conclusory statements do not sustain client's claims.

1. A national banking association is, by express provisions of sections 210 and 218 of the General Corporation Law, exempt, because such an association is a moneyed corporation, from their requirement that a foreign corporation doing business in the State obtain a certificate of authority to do business in the State.

2. Moreover, since a national bank is brought into existence under Federal legislation, it does not come within New York's statutory requirements limiting the right of foreign corporations to sue. Specific authority to bring this action in replevin is provided in the Federal National Bank Act (U. S. Code, tit. 12, § 24, subd. fourth). Such statute is paramount to the New York statute.

3. An attorney's conclusory statements, wholly on information and belief and [***2] unsupported by any factual showing by one having knowledge of the facts, do not sustain defendant's claims of plaintiff's lack of capacity to sue and insufficiency of plaintiff's cause of action.

Hesselgrave v. King


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


45 Misc. 2d 256; 256 N.Y.S.2d 753; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2357



January 18, 1965 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner policemen brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding seeking to declare invalid a local law enacted by respondent city insofar as it related to the residence requirements of policemen, and for incidental injunctive relief. The policemen were all appointed prior to July 1, 1961 and were all residents of the city upon their appointment. Subsequently, the policemen all obtained residency outside the city, but within the county.


OVERVIEW: The policemen contended that the local law requiring residency in the city for all policemen was invalid, because N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 30(4), which was effected prior to the local law at issue, exempted policemen from the residence requirements of local laws if certain conditions were found to exist, one being if the policemen were appointed prior to July 1, 1961. The court held that the local law was invalid and unconstitutional, because the local law went against the general law as provided for in § 30(4).


OUTCOME: The court held that the local law of the city requiring residency for the policemen was invalid and unconstitutional insofar as the policemen in the case were concerned.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- police -- Local Law No. 3 of 1964 of City of Peekskill, requiring policemen to be city residents, is invalid as to policemen who were appointed before July 1, 1961 and continue to reside in county (Public Officers Law, § 30, subd. 4; CPLR, art. 78).

Local Law No. 3 of 1964 of the City of Peekskill, requiring policemen of the city to be residents of the city or to become bona fide residents within 90 days, conflicts with a general State law and therefore is invalid as to the petitioners ( CPLR, art. 78), who were appointed prior to July 1, 1961 and who have resided in Westchester County at that time and ever since (Public Officers Law, § 30, subd. 4, pars. [1], [3]). A State statute is not local merely because it classifies a police force of more than 200 members differently from a force of less than 200 members.

Albert v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


45 Misc. 2d 87; 255 N.Y.S.2d 981; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2385



January 7, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, the motion of the respondents is granted, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individuals brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, requesting a hearing to determine whether respondents, Commissioner of Education of the State of New York and others, abused their discretion and acted arbitrarily and capriciously in a manner violative of the individuals' rights. The individuals sought a final order setting aside and declaring a nullity the failing results of examinations given to the individuals.


OVERVIEW: The individuals further sought an order directing respondents to change the examination to make it more appropriate for the practice of chiropractic. Respondents moved for an order, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(f), dismissing the petition on the ground that it was insufficient in law because it did not state facts sufficient to entitle the individuals to the relief demanded. The court rejected the individuals' claims that the questions were prepared to test the qualifications of doctors of medicine and in no way were applicable to the practice of chiropractic. The court held that N.Y. Educ. Law § 6552 did not limit the interrogations to only those subjects provided for in N.Y. Educ. Law § 6507, but mandated only the use of § 6507 questions on the examinations involving the subjects of anatomy, physiology, chemistry, pathology and diagnosis without precluding examinations on the additional basic subjects enumerated in N.Y. Educ. Law § 6552(1) such as hygiene and bacteriology. The court dismissed, holding that the petition failed to contain any allegations indicative of mandamus or particularly any allegations which established that respondents acted arbitrarily or capriciously.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondents' motion to dismiss the petition.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and surgeons -- chiropractors -- chiropractors must pass medical examinations in basic medical subjects (Education Law, §§ 6507, 6508, 6552).

Applicants for license as chiropractors must pass examinations not only in chiropractic but in the following "basic subjects": anatomy, physiology, chemistry, hygiene, bacteriology, pathology, and diagnosis; and the questions on those basic subjects may be the same as those used for doctors of medicine (Education Law, art. 132, § 6552, subds. 1, 2; art. 131, §§ 6507, 6508). This applies also to applicants who have been in practice in this State for less than seven years.

 

2231 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sherman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Broome County


47 Misc. 2d 335; 262 N.Y.S.2d 638; 1965 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2396



January 5, 1965 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The judgment of conviction is reversed, the information dismissed and the fine remitted to the appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Justice of the Peace of the Town of Vestal, Broome County, New York, which found defendant guilty of failing to yield the right of way, in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1143, and ordered him to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was prosecuted under § 1143, which required the driver of a vehicle about to enter a highway from a private road or driveway to "yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on said highway." Defendant claimed on appeal, among other things, that § 1143 was unconstitutional. The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that the version of § 1143 that was in effect at the time of defendant's trial was unconstitutionally vague. The court noted that a county court had declared the phrase "yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on said highway" to be vague in that it was unclear as to what constituted an approaching vehicle. The court also noted that the legislature recognized that the definition of the phrase "right of way," as found in the version of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 139 in effect at the time of defendant's trial, was itself vague and that the legislature amended § 139 to provide a more precise definition. Based on the county court's decision and the act of the legislature in amending § 139, the court concluded that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1143 was unconstitutional and, therefore, that defendant's conviction could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and dismissed the information.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- vehicle entering highway from driveway -- section 1143 of Vehicle and Traffic Law was unconstitutionally vague prior to amendment on October 1, 1964 of related section 139; conviction for violation which occurred before October 1, 1964, reversed and information dismissed.

 Section 1143 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, providing that "The driver of a vehicle about to enter or cross a highway from a private road or driveway shall yield the right of way to all vehicles approaching on said highway", was unconstitutionally vague, prior to October 1, 1964, when read in conjunction with former section 139 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which defined "right of way" as "The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway." However, effective October 1, 1964, former section 139 has been repealed and replaced with a more exact definition: "The right of one vehicle or pedestrian to proceed in a lawful manner in preference to another vehicle or pedestrian approaching under such circumstances of direction, speed and proximity as to give rise to danger of collision [***2] unless one grants precedence to the other." Thus, section 1143 is now constitutional and valid. But, a conviction for an alleged violation which occurred before October 1, 1964 must be reversed and the information dismissed.

 

2232 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Maurer v. Gross


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


45 Misc. 2d 13; 256 N.Y.S.2d 2; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1141



December 28, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a teacher and others, sought an order directing respondent superintendent and others to transfer the teacher from her present school to a school near her home and to pay her salary as a regular teacher until she was actually transferred to a new school. Intervenor unions sought dismissal of a portion of the teacher's cause and an order that the hearing be conducted in accordance with the collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: The teacher's application for a transfer was denied. She alleged that she was ready, willing, and able to resume her services as a teacher; and that the superintendent's failure to grant her a transfer was arbitrary, capricious, unjust, and illegal. The court held that under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 683 all public employees were given the right to representation in grievance procedures. The teacher had the right to have at the hearing scheduled before the superintendent of schools a representative of the City Teacher's Association to advance her grievance. In that respect, the court granted the teacher's petition. The court found no basis for a determination that the superintendent acted in an arbitrary, capricious, or illegal manner in deferring consideration of the transfer until after the third stage of the appeal. The court accordingly dismissed that portion of the proceeding without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court granted the teacher's petition to have the representation of her own choice. The court dismissed the portion of the petition that sought a transfer and paid salary.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- teachers -- despite exclusive collective bargaining agreement between Board of Education of City of New York and UFT, teacher is entitled at any stage of grievance procedure to change her representative from UFT to one of her own choosing (General Municipal Law, art. 16, §§ 682, 683, 683-a), which in this case is CTA -- but such teacher's request for "hardship transfer" to another school cannot be determined until her grievance appeal is determined.

1. Despite a purportedly exclusive collective bargaining agreement between the Board of Education of the City of New York and the United Federation of Teachers Local 2 American Federation of Teachers AFL-CIO (abbreviated as UFT), and despite the fact that petitioner teacher was represented by UFT in the first two stages of the grievance procedures provided for in said agreement, the teacher is entitled at the third stage or any stage of the grievance procedures or hearings to designate a different representative (General Municipal Law, art. 16, §§ 683, 683-a) -- in this case, the City Teachers' Association of New York (N. E. A.) (abbreviated as CTA). Article 16 of the General Municipal Law is not limited to grievance [***2] procedures established after October 1, 1963. The article (§ 682) does exclude the government of the City of New York, but it does not exclude the Board of Education of the city school district of New York. Section 683-a (added in 1964 to said article 16) is not a private or local bill. Said Board of Education and its Superintendent of Schools are directed to proceed with the third stage of petitioner's grievance appeal and to permit her to be represented at such hearing by a representative of CTA.

2. Petitioner also applies for a "hardship transfer" out of the school to which she is presently assigned, on the ground that the principal of said school is waging a campaign of harassment against her. However, the Superintendent of Schools cannot well determine this issue until her grievance appeal is heard and determined as above set forth. Therefore, this portion of petitioner's application is dismissed, without prejudice.

Mann v. Southold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


44 Misc. 2d 978; 255 N.Y.S.2d 308; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1150



December 23, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is accordingly denied and the temporary stay is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed a motion for an order to stay a criminal prosecution pending before a court of special sessions. The owner was charged with a violation of Southold, N.Y., Zoning Ordinances § 601 in that he had an automobile trailer on his property in violation of the ordinance. Defendant town sought to prosecute the owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner contended that the justice of the peace before whom the action was to have been tried was disqualified because of his interest in the subject of the prosecution. The justice of the peace was a member of the town board, which board enacted the zoning resolution. The court found that the mere fact that the justice of the peace, directly or indirectly, took part in the adoption of the resolution did not bar the court of special sessions from proceeding with the prosecution for violation of the ordinance. The New York Criminal Code provided for prosecution for the violation of an ordinance. The law directed that the prosecution be had before the court of special sessions in the town in which the alleged violation occurred.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion and vacated a temporary stay.


HEADNOTES

Judges -- disqualification -- Justice of Peace holding Court of Special Sessions in criminal prosecution, not disqualified because, as member of Town Board, he took part in adoption of ordinance with whose violation defendant is charged -- Court of Special Sessions has jurisdiction to determine constitutionality of ordinance -- motion to stay prosecution denied.

1. That a Justice of the Peace, as a member of a Town Board, took part, directly or indirectly, in the adoption of an ordinance, with whose violation defendant is charged in this criminal prosecution, does not disqualify him from holding a Court of Special Sessions to try the crime.

2. The Court of Special Sessions has jurisdiction to determine the constitutionality of the ordinance.

3. A motion to stay the prosecution is denied.
