Homeowners, not residents [***2] or property owners in a village whose Board of Appeals granted in 1962 to a corporation owning property on the north and east boundary lines of the village, a variance to construct a nine-hole pitch and putt golf course, are not "aggrieved" persons under section 179-b of the Village Law and therefore have no status to challenge the decisions of the Board of Appeals, even though their homes, outside the village are contiguous to the proposed golf course.

2. Even if they had status, they are barred from instituting a proceeding by the four-month limitation ( CPLR 217) as to the 1962 variance.

3. Section 179-b of the Village Law is not unconstitutional as depriving petitioners of their property without due process of law. Failure of petitioners to receive a notice of hearing, not provided for by section 179-b, did not deprive them of the enjoyment of their property; nor did the decision of the Board of Appeals permitting use of the borderline property as a pitch and putt golf course constitute a taking of petitioners' property, or a deprivation of the use and enjoyment thereof.

4. Any claim that the construction and operation of the golf course interferes with the use and enjoyment [***3] of petitioners' property should be asserted against the owner of the golf course.

 

2257 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Di Sano v. Storandt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


43 Misc. 2d 272; 250 N.Y.S.2d 701; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1663



June 12, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioners' motion to enjoin and restrain respondents from carrying into effect the Open Enrollment Plan and from implementing to resolution of the Board of Education adopted November 21, 1963, is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents moved to enjoin and restrain respondent board of education from carrying into effect an open enrollment plan and from implementing a resolution transferring students from one public school to another in the city to correct a racial imbalance.


OVERVIEW: The petition alleged that the receiving schools would become overcrowded; that citizens in the neighborhood of the receiving school would be deprived of their rights as parents and taxpayers; that the neighborhood school concept would be destroyed; that taxes would increase; that children would be transferred long distances from their resident areas; and that the students in a local school would be deprived of the proper facilities formerly available for educational purposes. Granting the motion, the court concluded that enough had been alleged to permit the granting of injunctive relief. The board's adoption of the plan and the subsequent implementation of it in sending and receiving students to and from different schools was clearly an unconstitutional exercise of power. The children attending a public school had a constitutional right to attend that school nearest their homes. They could not be compelled or arbitrarily forced to join a different ethnic group living miles away. Further, this was not a taxpayer's action against a school district, and it did not come within the rule that the board was not a municipal corporation within the meaning of N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 51.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- elimination of racial imbalance -- proceeding to enjoin Board of Education and Superintendent of Schools from operating "Open Enrollment Plan" and transferring students from one public school to another to correct racial imbalance is not taxpayer's action -- nor action under Education Law ( § 3813) -- petitioners not required to have preliminary hearing before Commissioner of Education -- petition alleges cause of action -- allegations to justify injunctive relief sufficient -- joining Superintendent of Schools as party is proper -- adoption of "Open Enrollment Plan" and transferring of pupils is unconstitutional and is enjoined.

1. A proceeding to enjoin a Board of Education and a Superintendent of Schools from operating an "Open Enrollment Plan" and transferring students from one public school to another for the purpose of correcting racial imbalance is not a taxpayer's action against the school district.

2. The proceeding is not an action pursuant to [***2] subdivision 1 of section 3813 of the Education Law and compliance with that section, including the filing of a verified claim, is not required.

3. As a proceeding under article 78 of the CPLR, petitioners are not required to have a preliminary hearing before the Commissioner of Education under section 310 of the Education Law. Moreover, the "Open Enrollment Plan" was adopted pursuant to the Commissioner's directive.

4. The petition alleges a cause of action.

5. The petition sufficiently alleges that petitioners will suffer irreparable harm as to justify the granting of injunctive relief.

6. The petition warranted joining the Superintendent of Schools as a party.

7. The adoption of the "Open Enrollment Plan" and the implementation thereof by transferring nonwhite pupils from one school to a school containing predominantly white pupils was an unconstitutional exercise of power. Children attending a public school have a constitutional right to attend a school nearest their homes and may not be compelled arbitrarily to join a different ethnic group living miles away. Racial imbalance is not constitutionally mandated. Carrying the "Open Enrollment Plan" into effect is enjoined.

 

2258 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Turco v. Union Free School Dist.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


43 Misc. 2d 367; 251 N.Y.S.2d 141; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1684



June 8, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was defendant school district's motion to dismiss plaintiffs residents' complaint, which sought a declaratory judgment to invalidate the adoption of a proposition to add an addition to the school district's high school.


OVERVIEW: The residents challenged the election on procedural grounds, and also asserted that the statutory qualifications for voting were unconstitutional. The court first held that it did not have jurisdiction, pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 2037, to consider the procedural matters because jurisdiction over those issues was vested in the Commissioner of Education. The court further concluded that the qualifications for voting were not unconstitutional. The court held that N.Y. Educ. Law § 2012, which required ownership of property or parentage of a child in school to vote, applied. The court found that N.Y. Const. art. II, § 1, which had minimal voting requirements, was only applied to general elections relating to governmental affairs of the whole state. The court ruled that the statutory requirements of N.Y. Educ. Law § 2012 were within the legislature's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- elections -- court has no jurisdiction to consider details of school election -- plaintiffs are aggrieved parties as to school election even though they did not attempt to vote -- section 2012 of Education Law adding requirement to qualifications of voters is not unconstitutional -- distinctions created by statute are within scope of legislative discretion.

1. Under section 2037 of the Education Law, only the Commissioner of Education and not the court has jurisdiction to consider such matters as the sufficiency of notice of the meeting, the supervision of the polls, the certification of the result of the voting, etc., with respect to an election.

2. In an action to declare invalid the adoption of a proposition to add an addition to the high school, plaintiffs are nonetheless aggrieved even though they did not register or attempt to vote.

3. Section 2012 of the Education Law, which adds a requirement to the qualifications of voters, that they own property in the school district or are parents of a child in school, is not unconstitutional as imposing greater restrictions on the right to vote than those provided in section 1 of article II of [***2] the Constitution. Section 1 of article II applies only to general elections relating to governmental affairs of the whole State.

4. The seemingly illogical distinctions created by section 2012 as between spouses of owners and spouses of lessees, etc., are within the scope of legislative discretion and present no constitutional question.

 

2259 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Dolan v. Krone


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


43 Misc. 2d 311; 250 N.Y.S.2d 496; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1691



June 5, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is accordingly dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, certain candidates who took a civil service competitive promotion examinations, instituted a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding in which they sought to have respondent, the Civil Service Commission of the State of New York, give them credit for answer "D" to a specific question. The Commission sought the dismissal of the petition. The court considered whether the question was susceptible of more than one answer.


OVERVIEW: The candidates, some of whom were not parties to the proceeding, took one of two examinations. One question was identical and required an identical answer. The examinations were conducted subject to a "pre-rating appeal procedure," which permitted a review of the examination by the candidates prior to any marking. A grader would then disclose the tentative key answers, and the candidates could object. All the party candidates selected answer "D." The grader also selected "D" as the tentative key answer. After some non-party candidates filed objections to the selection of answer "D," answer "C" was established as the final key answer. The party candidates asserted that the elimination of answer "D" and the acceptance of only answer "C" was arbitrary. Answer "D" contemplated the procedure set forth in N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 400, which had been declared unconstitutional; therefore, it was as if the statute had never been enacted. The court found that there was nothing ambiguous about the question. Because the question was susceptible of only one correct answer, which was answer "C," the rights of the non-party candidates would have been prejudiced if answer "D" was also acceptable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the candidates' petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- examinations -- tentative key answer to examination question was based on statute previously held unconstitutional -- final key answer took into consideration court ruling and was only correct answer -- petition asking that candidates be given credit for answer which agreed with tentative key answer dismissed.

Respondent Civil Service Commission selected as the tentative key answer to an examination question an answer based on a statute which previously had been held unconstitutional by the courts. Following objection by some of the candidates, the answer was changed, the final key answer taking the court ruling into consideration. Under the circumstances, the particular question is susceptible of only one correct answer. To direct respondents to accept another answer as equally correct would require them to act in an arbitrary and capricious manner. Accordingly, a petition by candidates who had chosen the same answer as that selected as the tentative key answer, asking that they be given credit for their answer, is dismissed.

 

2260 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Spahn v. Julian Messner, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


43 Misc. 2d 219; 250 N.Y.S.2d 529; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1711



May 28, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff baseball pitcher sought an injunction against the unauthorized publication of a book purporting to be his biography by defendants, a writer and a publisher, and for damages for injuries sustained by reason of the publication and distribution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff baseball player sought injunctive relief and damages from defendants, a writer and a publisher of an unauthorized biography about plaintiff, alleging that defendants were taking pecuniary advantage of plaintiff's name, photographs, likeness, and private life to create for profit a fictionalized and dramatic story. Plaintiff contended that his private life and the concomitant commercial exploitation of his name and likeness constituted an infringement of plaintiff's right of privacy. The trial court granted the injunction and awarded plaintiff damages, holding that publication of the book about plaintiff constituted a violation of the prohibitions of N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 51. Defendants never interviewed plaintiff or any member of his family, friends, or any baseball player who knew him. Also, the record unequivocally established that the book publicized areas of plaintiff's personal and private life, albeit inaccurate and distorted, and consisted of a host of factual errors, distortions, and fanciful passages.


OUTCOME: The court held that plaintiff baseball player was entitled to injunctive relief preventing the further publication and distribution of an unauthorized biography and was entitled to damages from defendants, the writer and publisher, for their violations of plaintiff's civil right to privacy.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil rights -- right of privacy -- fictionalization of life story of plaintiff baseball pitcher of wide renown, published without his consent, constituted invasion of plaintiff's right of privacy and abuse of public's limited privilege to inquire into individual's life.

A fictionalization of the life story of plaintiff, a baseball pitcher of wide renown and acclaim, published without his consent, the inclusion in the book of aspects of his private life and the commercial exploitation of his name and likeness constitute an infringement of plaintiff's right of privacy in violation of sections 50 and 51 of the Civil Rights Law. Defendants, the publisher and author of the book, have intruded upon plaintiff's solitude and into his private affairs, have disclosed embarrassing "facts" about plaintiff, placed plaintiff in a false light in the public eye and appropriated, for their advantage, plaintiff's name and likeness. The distortions, inaccuracies, invented dialogue, and the narration of happenings out of context, clearly indicate, at the very least, a careless disregard for the responsibility of the press and an abuse of the public's limited privilege to inquire into an individual's [***2] life. The purported biography transgresses the bounds of legitimate public interest by its breadth of reportorial coverage of those areas of plaintiff's life, such as his deeply personal relationships with members of his immediate family and his introspective thoughts, which defy classification as public. Plaintiff is granted an injunction preventing further publication and distribution of the book and damages of $ 10,000.

 

2261 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Loew v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


43 Misc. 2d 1021; 252 N.Y.S.2d 493; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1727



May 26, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a motion for a temporary injunction restraining completion of a proposed affiliation contract between a third hospital and defendants, the City of New York, New York, the Commissioner of Hospitals of the City of New York, New York, and a first hospital. Defendants' existing affiliation contract concerned medical care and related services at a second hospital.


OVERVIEW: Defendants asserted that hospitals that were affiliated with medical schools or voluntary teaching hospitals provided the best care. The taxpayer asserted that the enabling legislation, New York City, N.Y., Charter § 583-a, was unconstitutional because it unlawfully delegated legislative power to the Commissioner without any policy or guidelines. The court held that the taxpayer's attempt to restrain defendants from entering into another affiliation contract did not warrant injunctive relief pendente lite. The court found that the Commissioner had the power to furnish hospital services under New York City, N.Y., Charter § 583-a and to do so through contracts under New York City, N.Y., Charter § 583-a(b). The court ruled that no principle affecting a constitutional grant of that power could invalidate its accomplishment by means of the contract. The Commissioner did not legislate the performance of services under the contract, but delegated them, and the contract did not impair the Commissioner's ability to provide the services. The Commissioner could contract for services that would have been inadequate without association with a medical school or voluntary teaching hospital.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- municipal hospitals -- New York City Commissioner of Hospitals may make contract affiliating municipal hospital with voluntary teaching hospital (New York City Charter, §§ 583-a, 583-b, 587); legislative power and police power not unconstitutionally delegated, taxpayer's application for injunction denied.

Medical school graduates are unwilling to accept internships in hospitals which are not affiliated with either a medical school or a voluntary teaching hospital. The City of New York maintains hospitals for the care of the indigent ill, and 11 of those municipal hospitals are not thus affiliated, and the result in those hospitals has been a steady deterioration of medical care and a loss of the accreditation certificate of the Joint Commission on Accreditation. In this emergency, the city's Commissioner of Hospitals with the approval of the city's Board of Hospitals and the city's Board of Estimate has properly made contracts affiliating certain municipal hospitals with a voluntary teaching hospital (New York City Charter, §§ 583-a, 583-b, 587). It cannot be fairly said that the cited sections unconstitutionally delegate [***2] legislative power to the Commissioner without sufficient guidelines, or that the contracts unconstitutionally delegate municipal police powers to the voluntary hospital. In this taxpayer's suit, the plaintiff's motion for a temporary injunction against performance of the contracts is denied.

 

2262 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Lonschein v. Warden, Queens House of Detention for Men


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


43 Misc. 2d 109; 250 N.Y.S.2d 15; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1729



May 25, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The writ is therefore dismissed and the District Attorney is directed to submit a judgment on this determination (see, CPLR 7010, subd. [c]).it


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus on behalf of defendant, who had been convicted of murder in the first degree and sentenced to death. The attorney challenged the legality of the detention on the ground that changes in the law were ex post facto and could not be applied to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murder in its first degree in the death of a payroll guard during a robbery and, along with his codefendant, was ordered to be executed. The judgment was reversed on appeal and a new trial was ordered after there was a statutory amendment to the basic punishment for murder in the first degree under N.Y. Penal Law § 1045(1). Defendant then challenged the legality of his detention on the ground that the changes in the law were ex post facto and could not be applied to him, and his attorney filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus on his behalf. The court dismissed the writ, holding that the mere statutory change, which substituted the finding of a jury for that of a judge, could not be held to be unconstitutional as an ex post facto law and a law which changed punishment was not in and of itself an ex post facto law unless that change inflicted a greater or additional punishment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the attorney's application for writ of habeas corpus on behalf of defendant, who had been convicted of murder in the first degree and had been sentenced to death.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- ex post facto laws -- challenge to legality of law as ex post facto is not premature -- changes in law dealing with punishment for murder in first degree effective on defendant's new trial, eliminated death penalty, except that, if Judge did not sentence to life imprisonment, jury which found defendant guilty, could be reconvened and jury could decide whether to sentence to life imprisonment or death and in that proceeding any evidence, even if otherwise excludible, shall be received; statute is not ex post facto because of kind of evidence admissible in proceeding subsequent to trial -- sentence of life imprisonment is less than sentence of death and therefore change in law is not ex post facto law.

1. A change in the law dealing with punishment for the crime of murder in the first degree became effective July 1, 1963, shortly before defendant's conviction for the crime of murder in the first degree, allegedly committed on May 10, 1961, was reversed by the Court of Appeals (13 N Y 2d 148) and a new trial ordered, to [***2] which trial the new statute is applicable. A challenge to the legality of defendant's detention on the ground that the law is ex post facto as to defendant is not premature. The validity of the statute is determinable by reference to what may happen thereunder in any alternative and not merely by reference to what verdict actually results upon the trial.

2. The changes eliminate the mandatory death penalty formerly applicable to a common-law conviction for deliberate and premeditated murder or upon a jury's failure to recommend life imprisonment upon a conviction for felony murder. The basic punishment for murder in the first degree is life imprisonment but, if the court does not punish by life imprisonment, it shall "conduct a proceeding to determine whether defendant should be sentenced to life imprisonment or to death * * * with the jury that found defendant guilty" ( Penal Law, § 1045-a, subd. 2). In such proceeding (subd. 3) "Any relevant evidence, not legally privileged, shall be received regardless of its admissibility under the exclusionary rules of evidence." The statute is not ex post facto because of the different kind of evidence permissible at the second stage portion [***3] of the trial. The evidence admissible in the sentencing proceeding does not affect the type of evidence required to prove defendant's guilt and such evidence is pertinent only after a verdict of guilt. Even under the prior procedure, where the jury recommended life imprisonment, the court was not bound by such recommendation and, in order to determine whether to impose life imprisonment, the court could examine defendant's record and any otherwise inadmissible evidence. Thus there is no basic change in the type of evidence to be considered under the sentencing power.

3. A law which changes punishment is not, in and of itself, an ex post facto law unless that change inflicts a greater or additional punishment or affects the offender unfavorably. A sentence of life imprisonment is lesser punishment than a sentence of death and, therefore, the changes in the law are not ex post facto.

 

2263 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rosenstiel v. Rosenstiel


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


43 Misc. 2d 462; 251 N.Y.S.2d 565; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1759



May 18, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband brought an action against defendant wife for annulment of their marriage.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that the wife's prior Mexican divorce was void under New York law. The wife argued that the divorce was valid and that res judicata applied. The court noted that res judicata as a defense could be invoked only where the same parties and issues were before the court and the contested issues were definitively determined on the merits, determined that any findings by the Mexican courts could not operate as res judicata in New York, and dismissed the defense on the facts and as a matter of law. The court pointed out that contrary to the domestic concept of the marital res and jurisdiction predicated upon domicile, submission of the parties to the power of the court was the source of jurisdiction to grant a divorce in Mexico, and noted that the wife and her former husband violated the express interdiction of N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 51, which forbade agreements between a husband and wife to alter or dissolve the marriage. The court stated that unless one of the parties was domiciled in the divorcing state, its court had no power to hear the merits of the controversy, and concluded that the Mexican decree had no validity in New York and would not be recognized.


OUTCOME: The court directed judgment in favor of the husband, and a hearing with respect to alimony and counsel fee, which the court decreed the wife was entitled to recover.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Husband and wife -- foreign divorce -- attorney-client privilege not waived by plaintiff's instituting action against attorney for accounting -- decree of Mexican court reinstating divorce decree obtained by defendant's prior husband is not res judicata since validity of Mexican decree under New York law was not involved -- Mexican divorce decree obtained by defendant's prior husband was pursuant to agreement with defendant in violation of section 51 of Domestic Relations Law, was not based upon domicile, and is invalid -- plaintiff is awarded decree annulling marriage to defendant.

1. Testimony, privileged because of the attorney-client relationship, was not admitted. The privilege was not waived by plaintiff's instituting an action against the attorney for an accounting and other relief.

2. In this action to annul a marriage on the ground that a prior Mexican divorce obtained by defendant wife's prior husband was a nullity, an ex parte "incidente" proceeding allegedly commenced by plaintiff under another name in Mexico resulted in a decree nullifying the prior husband's divorce. Defendant then filed an "amparo" in the Mexican Federal Court which was upheld on appeal and [***2] effected a reinstatement of the divorce decree. The order reinstating the divorce is not res judicata since it made no finding with respect to the validity of the divorce decree obtained by defendant's prior husband. The order of reinstatement was predicated on lack of notice to defendant of the "incidente" proceeding. The Mexican appeals court had no power under Mexican law to decide the issue of the validity of the divorce on the merits. Moreover, even if it determined the merits and the person who instituted the "incidente" proceeding were plaintiff, the decree would not be res judicata since the validity of the divorce under New York law was not in issue.

3. Defendant and her prior husband agreed in New York to divorce each other. An attorney was engaged to effectuate the divorce who paid the fee of the Mexican attorney representing defendant and the Mexican attorney representing the husband. The husband entered Mexico, signed a register, signed papers written in Spanish and returned to the United States within one hour. He never became a domiciliary of Mexico. The decree of divorce recited that the court had jurisdiction because the husband signed the register [***3] and both parties submitted to the jurisdiction of the court. Since domicile is not recognized by the Mexican decree, the divorce is invalid. Moreover defendant and her first husband violated section 51 of the Domestic Relations Law which forbids any agreement between a husband and wife to alter or dissolve the marriage by their collusive agreement.

4. Plaintiff is awarded a decree annulling his marriage to defendant.

 

2264 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Levy v. Power


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


43 Misc. 2d 158; 250 N.Y.S.2d 511; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1768



May 14, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed a petition for an order declaring N.Y. Elec. Law § 242-a (1964) unconstitutional and requiring respondent board of elections to set up the ballot in the June 2, 1964, primary election in blocks, rather than slates.


OVERVIEW: The candidate claimed that the statute was discriminatory and prejudicial in that it deprived him of equal protection of the law because it gave preference to candidates who were part of a full slate by placing them on the first position on the ballot and relegated those candidates with less than a full slate to succeeding positions. The court determined that the legislature was within its authority to mandate the position of a candidate's name on the voting machine if the candidate was part of a slate and that its action to simplify the machine was fair, equitable, and reasonable. The court dismissed the petition and held that the candidate had failed to demonstrate the statute's unconstitutionality because it gave all candidates an opportunity to present an entire slate or to associate with others to become part of a slate. The court concluded that the candidate's contention of unequal protection of the law was meritless because all candidates had the same right to become members of a slate and thus to obtain the alleged preferred position on the machine.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- position on ballot -- statute (L. 1964, ch. 936) giving preference on ballot on voting machine to candidates who are part of full slate is constitutional.

Subdivision 7 of section 242-a of the Election Law (as added by L. 1964, ch. 936), the effect of which is to place candidates who are part of a full slate on the first line on the ballot upon the voting machine and those with less than a full slate to lower lines on the ballot is constitutional. The right given to all candidates to become members of a slate and thus obtain preferred positions on the machine provides equal protection of the law to all.

 

2265 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Griffin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


42 Misc. 2d 1050; 249 N.Y.S.2d 801; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1803



May 5, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Under the circumstances, the motion of the defendant for an order dismissing the prior offense information filed against him herein is granted unless the District Attorney shall desire a hearing for the purpose of either establishing that the defendant was in fact represented by counsel or that he consciously and knowingly waived his right to counsel, being cognizant of his constitutional rights to have counsel appointed for him ( People v. Sabatino, 41 Misc 2d 170; People v. Crimi, 278 App. Div. 997, affd. 303 N. Y. 749).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a criminal trial, defendant filed a motion for an order dismissing a prior offense information filed against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of an offense in another state. In a criminal trial, he filed a motion for an order dismissing the prior offense information filed against him by the district attorney. The court held that where the foreign conviction was obtained when the foreign court had a policy of not appointing counsel to indigents, such conviction was obtained in violation of defendant's rights for the purposes of N.Y. Penal Law § 1943, which provided that no prior conviction would be utilized as a predicate for multiple offender treatment if such conviction was obtained in violation of the accused's rights.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion unless the District Attorney sought a hearing to determine whether defendant was in fact represented by counsel or that he consciously and knowingly waived his right to counsel.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- multiple offender punishment -- conviction in violation of constitutional rights -- under 1964 amendment to section 1943 of Penal Law prior offense information is dismissed where conviction was obtained in violation of defendant's constitutional rights.

A prior offense information is dismissed under the amendment to section 1943 of the Penal Law effected by chapter 446 of the Laws of 1964, where defendant shows that his prior North Carolina conviction was obtained in violation of his constitutional rights in that he had no attorney, had no funds to hire one, and one was not assigned to represent him.

 

2266 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Havern


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Washington County


43 Misc. 2d 430; 251 N.Y.S.2d 350; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1806



May 4, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the People of the State of New York, questioned the application of N.Y. Correct. Law §§ 615 through 619 (1959), which repealed former N.Y. Correct. Law §§ 615 through 623. Defendants argued that they were entitled to the return and destruction of their fingerprints and photographs upon demanding the same from the state police and the department of correction.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were adjudged to be youthful offenders. Defendants sought the return of their fingerprints and photographs from the department of correction. N.Y. Correct. Law § 944 (1960) provided that upon acquittal, a person charged was entitled to the return of fingerprints and photographs from a police officer, sheriff, peace officer, or a member of any police department. The department was not a police officer, sheriff, peace officer, or a member of any police department. However, the court found that the very purpose of § 944 and N.Y. Penal Law § 516 would be frustrated if the department were allowed to retain the fingerprints and photographs as a part of their permanent records. The court concluded that the photographs and fingerprints of the persons adjudged to be youthful offenders were to be retained as confidential matter in the files of the department of correction and would not be returned to such persons. The court held that there was no duty to return the photographs and fingerprints because the statutes provided for their return only upon the determination of a pending criminal action or proceeding against a person in favor of such person.


OUTCOME: The court held that the photographs and fingerprints of persons adjudged to be youthful offenders were to be retained as confidential matter in the files of the department of correction and would not be returned.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- youthful offenders -- persons charged with felonies and later convicted as youthful offenders are not entitled to return and destruction of fingerprints and photographs from Department of Correction and State Police.

A person with no prior criminal record who is photographed and fingerprinted upon being charged with a felony, and who is later adjudged to be a youthful offender, is not entitled to the return and destruction of his fingerprints and photographs upon demanding same from the State Police and the Department of Correction. Under section 913-o of the Code of Criminal Procedure the fingerprints and photographs of such persons are retained as confidential matter in the files of the Department of Correction and shall not be returned to such persons. The State Police are under no duty to return fingerprints and photographs taken by them of a person charged with a felony and who is later adjudged a youthful offender because section 944 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and section 516 of the Penal Law provide for their return only upon the determination of a pending criminal action or proceeding against a person in favor of such person.

 

2267 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Buchko v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


43 Misc. 2d 43; 249 N.Y.S.2d 823; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1833



April 24, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiffs' cross motion for summary judgment is perforce denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school district taxpayers and voters, filed for declaratory judgment, an injunction, and other relief against defendant school board regarding alleged illegal acts of the board. The issue before the court was the school board's motion for summary judgment pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3211(c) and its motion to dismiss pursuant N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 3211(a)(2) and (5) for lack of jurisdiction and failing to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: When the school board consolidated two separate union free school districts into a single central district, the taxpayers argued that first, the board violated N.Y. Educ. Law § 1523(5) because, in part, the action was done without public notice. Second, because the consolidation was only intended to consolidate each district's debts, which unconstitutionally deprived the taxpayers of their property rights and imposed illegal taxes. Third, the board was transporting pupils among the former separate districts in violation of N.Y. Educ. Law § 1805. The court held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction as to only one count. It held that an appeal to the Commissioner of Education was the exclusive remedy where the validity of a district meeting was in dispute. But the court held that the other causes of action involved the determination of the legality or constitutionality of the acts of public officials or the interpretation of statutes and were all within the jurisdiction of the court for declaratory judgment. But the court granted the board's motion as to all three counts for failing to state a claim because the pleadings consisted of only conclusory allegations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the school board's motion to dismiss on jurisdictional grounds as to only one count; on all other counts the motion to dismiss on jurisdictional grounds was denied. However, the court granted the school board's motion to dismiss for failing to state a cause of action as to all three counts but gave the taxpayers leave to refile. The taxpayers' cross-motion for summary judgment was denied.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- consolidation and centralization -- consolidation may be followed almost immediately by centralization (Education Law, §§ 1510-1513; §§ 1801, 1805; cf. §§ 1517, 1518, 1523, subd. 5) -- however, validity of request for consolidation (Education Law, § 1511, subd. 1) and of Commissioner of Education's approval thereof may be attacked by action for declaratory judgment.

1. Two union free school districts were consolidated (pursuant to Education Law, §§ 1510 to 1513), and, about a month later, the Commissioner of Education validly made an order laying out the territory of this newly consolidated union free school district as a central school district (pursuant to Education Law, § 1801). Said order was not made too soon; section 1523 (subd. 5) of the Education Law is inapplicable. Allegations, in this complaint by taxpayers and voters, that the sole purpose was to consolidate the debt burdens of the districts (cf. Education Law, §§ 1517, 1518) and that plaintiffs are subjected to illegally levied taxes (cf. Education Law, § 1804, subds. 5, 6) and have been unconstitutionally deprived of property [***2] rights, are conclusory and insufficient. Plaintiffs also allege that defendant board of education has discontinued the use of certain elementary school buildings and is transferring pupils among the buildings in the former separate districts, in violation of section 1805 of the Education Law; but, if the consolidation prior to the centralization was valid, section 1805 is inapplicable. The only steps in the consolidation procedure in this case which may be attacked are the validity of the original request for consolidation (Education Law, § 1511, subd. 1) and the Commissioner's approval of the proposed consolidation. Accordingly, the complaint is dismissed ( CPLR 3211, subd. [a], par. 7), without prejudice to an application for leave to replead if so advised.

2. Although an appeal to the Commissioner of Education is the exclusive remedy in the first instance to resolve a dispute as to the validity of a district meeting or the proceedings thereat (Education Law, § 2037), an action for a declaratory judgment is proper, and is perhaps the only remedy, to determine a controversy involving the validity of multiple acts of the Commissioner of Education, District Superintendent of [***3] Schools, boards of education, and electors of districts, resulting in consolidation and centralization.

 

2268 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Swarts v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


42 Misc. 2d 761; 249 N.Y.S.2d 44; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1835



April 24, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents brought an action against defendant board of education (board) seeking an injunction preventing the board from refusing to enroll the parents' children pending the result of an action challenging an action of the board to charge tuition to the children.


OVERVIEW: The parents' children and others living in the same area, had attended the board's schools for nearly 45 years when the board decided to charge tuition to children living in that area. The parents brought an action challenging the tuition and filed an application for a preliminary injunction preventing the board from refusing to enroll the children pending the outcome of the action. The court granted the injunction, holding that the status quo of the children attending the schools tuition free should have been maintained until a final decision was reached on the merits. The potential irreparable harm for the parents outweighed the damage to or inconvenience of the board; therefore, the court was within its discretion to grant the preliminary injunction against the board.


OUTCOME: The court granted the parents' preliminary injunction preventing the board from refusing to enroll the students pending the result of the action challenging the charging of the tuition.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Injunctions -- temporary injunction -- where school districts were annexed to City of Rochester, legislation providing that students could attend city schools without tuition, temporary injunction is granted against city to restrain it from charging tuition pursuant to local law to become effective on September 1, 1964.

As a result of chapter 547 of the Laws of 1918 and chapter 519 of the Laws of 1922, school districts in certain towns were annexed by the City of Rochester, the legislation providing that students in the towns would attend schools in the city without the payment of tuition. By local law to become effective September 1, 1964 the city provided that students from such districts could attend city schools on condition that they paid stated tuition charges. In this action for an injunction, plaintiffs demonstrate that they will suffer irreparable damage and that there exists a clear legal right to a temporary injunction. The arrangement has been in effect for nearly 45 years. The irreparable harm which plaintiffs and the affected children will suffer is not commensurate with the inconvenience to be suffered by defendants. In the exercise of discretion the court [***2] grants a temporary injunction to maintain the status quo until final determination of the action.

 

2269 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Babylon v. Stengel


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


43 Misc. 2d 196; 250 N.Y.S.2d 514; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1849



April 22, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town brought a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to compel respondent, the Suffolk County Civil Service Commission, to jurisdictionally classify the position of Assistant Public Welfare Officer of the Town of Babylon in the exempt class of the classified civil service, rather than in the competitive class.


OVERVIEW: The town appointed a provisional town public welfare officer after the first officer retired. The Commission established an eligible list for the position, which did not include the provisional appointee. The town's application asserted that the legislature had jurisdictionally classified the position of assistant town public welfare officer in the exempt class. Finding that no issues of fact were presented, the court dismissed the petition. Under N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6, all appointments to positions in the civil service had to be made according to merit and fitness to be ascertained as far as practicable by competitive examination. The legislature and various civil service commissions could provide otherwise, classifying positions in the classified service as exempt or noncompetitive when it was not practicable to fill such positions by competitive examination within the limits of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law §§ 40-44. The position of assistant town public welfare officer was not one of those described in § 41, nor did the town contend that it was an office or position for the filling of which a competitive or noncompetitive examination could be found to be not practicable.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- classification -- position of Assistant Town Public Welfare Officer not required to be placed in exempt class because statute authorizing creation of position provides that incumbent hold office during pleasure of Town Board -- town is aggrieved party with standing to bring proceeding to compel Civil Service Commission to classify position in exempt class.

1. A town authorized its Supervisor to act as Town Public Welfare Officer (Social Welfare Law, § 67, subd. 1) and then created the position of Assistant Town Public Welfare Officer. Classification of such position in the exempt class is not required because subdivision 1 of section 67 of the Social Welfare Law provides that "employees shall hold office during the pleasure of the town board". Under section 6 of article V of the Constitution, positions must be placed in the competitive class unless it is not practicable to fill such positions by competitive examination. The Legislature may not classify a particular position in the exempt class unless it is one for which ascertainment of merit and fitness, or the filling of which, by competitive examination, is not practicable.  [***2] There is no express language in section 67 placing the position in the exempt class. The tenure of the appointee is subject to the provisions of the Civil Service Law.

2. Petitioner town is an aggrieved party and has standing to bring this proceeding to compel the Civil Service Commission to classify the position in the exempt class.

 

2270 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Golly


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


43 Misc. 2d 122; 250 N.Y.S.2d 210; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1858



April 20, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's application for a copy of his testimony before the Grand Jury is granted (see People v. Kresel, 142 Misc. 88).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, indicted for perjury in the first degree, filed a motion for discovery and inspection of any eavesdropping evidence that may have been used before the grand jury, for its suppression, and for a bill of particulars.


OVERVIEW: The sole factual allegation which defendant urged in support of his motion was that a conversation with his former attorney about which he was alleged to have lied to the grand jury took place without any witnesses to it. Inasmuch as under New York law, there had to either be two witnesses to support a charge of perjury or strong corroborative evidence of the testimony of a witness, defendant implied that the district attorney must have presented evidence to the grand jury gained by electronic eavesdropping of his conversation with his attorney. The court held that defendant was not entitled to raise questions concerning the constitutionality of the electronic eavesdropping evidence heard by the grand jury by motion in the motion part but was required to present his intentions in the trial part. Moreover, the court held that a motion made in a motion part to discover and suppress eavesdropping evidence would be denied as there was no general right of discovery and defendant would suffer no prejudice in awaiting trial before challenging the constitutionality of evidence. Finally, the court held that the application for testimony before the grand jury would be granted.


OUTCOME: Defendant's application for a copy of his testimony before the grand jury was granted.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to discovery -- in criminal case, no general right to discovery exists -- motion to discover improperly made in motion part; issues of constitutionality of eavesdropping evidence must await trial -- motion for bill of particulars of items of evidentiary nature is denied -- defendant entitled to copy of testimony before Grand Jury upon payment of fee.

1. There is no general right to a discovery in a criminal action.

2. The motion to discover raises issues of constitutionality which can be resolved, not in a motion part of the court, but at a Trial Term. Since defendant will suffer no undue prejudice in awaiting trial before challenging the constitutionality of eavesdropping evidence which he supposes will be used against him, his motion to discover and suppress is denied.

3. Defendant's motion for a bill of particulars of items of an evidentiary nature is denied.

4. Defendant's application for a copy of his testimony before the Grand Jury is granted and a copy is directed to be turned over to him upon payment of the fee.

 

2271 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Municipal Lien Corp. v. Gawronski


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


42 Misc. 2d 369; 248 N.Y.S.2d 318; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1904



April 2, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The relief sought herein is denied and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding brought pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioner bidder sought an order declaring a tax sale held by respondent county commissioner of finance to be null and void and directing a resale.


OVERVIEW: The bidder claimed that the sale was illegal on the grounds that it was in bulk and not by individual items. The court disagreed. The difference between a bulk sale and one by individual items was that in a bulk sale a bidder had to make a bulk bid for the entire delinquent tax roll rather than bid separately on each piece of property. The subject sale was advertised as a sale by individual items and not as a bulk sale. Were it not for the decision of the county to bid for all of the parcels, individual parcels could have been sold. The bid of the county made by the commissioner was pursuant to § 7-7.0 of the Erie County Tax Act and in pursuance to the terms of a resolution and in pursuance to the terms of a resolution of the Board of Supervisors in which the commissioner offered to purchase all the parcels of real estate. Because there were thousands of parcels on which taxes were owed and since the county intended to purchase each parcel, it would have been a useless waste of time to read each parcel and the amount owed on it.


OUTCOME: The court denied the relief sought and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- tax liens, tax sales and tax titles -- Erie County Tax Act validly prefers county over other bidders, and allows county to bid in all properties with one total bid, and allows judicial proceedings by owners only and not by mere bidders -- decisions construing Real Property Tax Law inapplicable.

1. The Erie County Tax Act (L. 1942, ch. 812, as amd., §§ 7-4.0, 7-6.0, 7-7.0, 7-11.0, 14-6.0) validly provides, as to tax sales, that "The county treasurer may prescribe reasonable rules and regulations to expedite and govern the conduct of such sale and such rules and regulations shall be set forth in * * * pamphlet and shall be binding upon all persons attending such sale" and that "each parcel shall be sold for a sum sufficient to pay all the taxes, fees, penalties, interest and charges", and that "The county of Erie may become a purchaser at any such sale and the offer of the county to purchase any parcel of land shall be preferred over all other offers made for the same" and that "No tax sale * * * shall be enjoined or * * * vacated except upon a proceeding brought therefor by the owner of such real [***2] property" and that any invalidity of any part of this law shall not affect the rest of the law. Accordingly, for a tax sale of 6,738 separate parcels, each parcel and its owner and the total amount of tax charges on each parcel were listed; but the county Board of Supervisors by a resolution authorized its Commissioner of Finance to bid in, on behalf of the county, all of the parcels for the tax charges thereon; and, accordingly, the notice of sale stated that the Commissioner would purchase for the county all of the parcels. Accordingly, it would have been a waste of time to conduct separate sales of each parcel. The Commissioner made one bid of $ 862,652.03 for the 6,738 parcels and thus properly bought them all for the county.

2. The Erie County Tax Act validly prefers the county over other bidders. There is no constitutional requirement that a tax sale be public, or be made by individual parcels. Moreover, this proceeding (under CPLR, art. 78) is brought, not by a property owner, but a bidding stranger.

3. Decisions construing the Real Property Tax Law ( § 1006; § 1008, subd. 3) as preferring a bid of the full amount of the tax charges on a parcel for a nine-tenths interest [***3] in the parcel, over a bid for the entire parcel or for all the parcels, do not apply to the quite differently worded provisions of the Erie County Tax Act.

 

2272 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Strippoli v. Bickal


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Monroe County


42 Misc. 2d 475; 248 N.Y.S.2d 588; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1909



April 1, 1964 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petitioners' motion to enjoin and restrain the respondents from proceeding with or carrying out the transfer of students from Public School No. 3 to Public School No. 30 is granted and the determination of the Board of Education to that end is annulled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, parents of public school students, filed a petition and show cause order against respondent board of education resulting in a proceeding for an injunction referred to the court. The action was the result of the board's attempt to transfer students from one public school in the district to another.


OVERVIEW: Several parents of school children filed a proceeding against the board of education for an injunction relating to a proposed transfer of students from one public school to another. The board argued that the purpose of the transfer was to alleviate overcrowding at a particular school. The parents argued that the transfers were effectuated to cure racial imbalance in the schools. The board argued that the parents were required to first prosecute an appeal to the State Commissioner of Education. The board also argued that the parents and their children were not aggrieved parties and thus could not bring the action. The court held that an initial appeal before the commissioner was unnecessary. Further, persons other than transferees had standing to bring the proceeding to enjoin violation of the statute. Each child had a right to attend only the public school in the district in which he resided. The court found that the Constitution did not require that there had to be an intermingling of the races in all school districts. The court held that the transfer was an arbitrary act and exceeded the bounds of sound discretion. As such, the act was set aside and enjoined.


OUTCOME: The court granted the parents' motion to enjoin and restrain the board from transferring students from one public school to another.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- elimination of racial imbalance -- transfer of nonwhite pupils of one school by bus to second school two and one-half miles away was effected to cure racial imbalance rather than to relieve overcrowding -- parents of white pupils in second school, alleging violation of constitutional rights, are not required to appeal to Commissioner of Education and have standing as aggrieved parties, to bring proceeding to annul action of school authorities -- respondents violated section 3201 of Education Law by excluding colored pupils from first school -- respondents unconstitutionally transferred non-white pupils; petitioners are entitled to restrain transfers and to annul respondents' determination.

1. The fifth and sixth grades in a neighborhood school containing pupils, 95.3% of whom were nonwhite, were transferred in the middle of the school year by bus to another neighborhood school two and one-half miles distant [***2] whose pupils were all white, and the fifth and sixth grades of that school were commingled so as to produce white and nonwhite pupils in each class. Such transfer was effected to cure racial imbalance, rather than to relieve overcrowding as claimed by the school authorities.

2. The parents of the white pupils in the second neighborhood school who allege that the transfer violates their constitutional rights are not required to appeal to the Commissioner of Education first but have standing as aggrieved parties, to bring this proceeding to annul the action of the Board of Education, even though they are persons other than the transferred pupils or their parents.

3. Section 3201 of the Education Law provides that no person shall be refused admission to or be excluded from any public school on account of race, creed, color or national origin. Respondents violated said section by excluding the pupils from the first school because of their color.

4. Under the New York (art. I, § 11) and Federal (14th Amdt.) Constitutions, a child should not be enrolled or transported to a certain schoolhouse because he is white or colored. The transferred children had no constitutionally guaranteed [***3] right to attend a school outside the attendance area in which they resided. By the transfer, respondents exercised power unconstitutionally. Desegregation of schools as mandated by the United States Supreme Court does not mean that Negro children who live in a noncontiguous area must be bussed into a white area in order to desegregate a school attended by white pupils. The children of that school have an equal right to attend the school nearest their homes uninterrupted by an arbitrarily forced infusion of another ethnic group living two and one-half miles away. Petitioners are entitled to restrain respondents from proceeding with the transfer of students and their determination to so do is annulled.

 

2273 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wasmuth v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


43 Misc. 2d 14; 250 N.Y.S.2d 11; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1922



March 27, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractors, suing on behalf of themselves and others similarly situated, filed an action against defendants, the Commissioner of Education of the State of New York and others, seeking a preliminary injunction against the Commissioner's enforcement of various sections of N.Y. Educ. Law art. 132, and a declaration that the statutes were unconstitutional. The Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statutes required new chiropractors, as prerequisite to obtaining a license to practice, and those with a certain number of years of experience to take: (1) the same examination given applicants for medical certificates in anatomy, physiology, chemistry, hygiene, bacteriology, pathology, and diagnosis; and (2) an examination in the use and effects of X-ray. The statutes also required chiropractors of greater experience to take an examination in fundamentals of anatomy and physiology. The chiropractors claimed that the statutes were discriminatory and that the examinations were a test of medical, rather than chiropractic knowledge, and were therefore inappropriate. The court ruled that the statutes were constitutional. Chiropractors treated the sick and made referrals to medical personnel. The legislature was warranted in not taking chances and in requiring chiropractors to prove their knowledge of the subject matters of the examinations. The statutes conferred on chiropractors privileges which, the state's highest court had determined, they could not claim as a matter of constitutional right. This was ample to meet the challenge that they were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Commissioner's motion to dismiss and denied the chiropractors' motion for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Physicians and surgeons -- examination as prerequisite to licensing of chiropractors -- Education Law (art. 132) requiring examinations as prerequisite to licensing of chiropractors is constitutional.

Sections of article 132 of the Education Law which require examinations as a prerequisite to licensing chiropractors are constitutional. The Legislature was warranted in requiring chiropractors to prove their knowledge of the use and effects of X rays, and to require that they show some knowledge of anatomy, physiology, chemistry, hygiene, bacteriology, pathology and diagnosis as specified in the article. The challenged statute confers on chiropractors privileges which they could not otherwise claim as a matter of constitutional right.

 

2274 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mastrangelo v. State Council of Parks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


42 Misc. 2d 650; 249 N.Y.S.2d 19; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1942



March 24, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 petition against respondents, a state conservation commissioner, other state officials, a city mayor, and other city officials, that sought an annulment of certain action and an injunction against other actions against a proposed acquisition of their property for a park expansion. The state and city officials moved to dismiss the petition on grounds of legal insufficiency.


OVERVIEW: City officials adopted actions in connection with a proposed acquisition and condemnation of the owner's properties for an extension of a city park, which included an application to state officials for state aid for the costs of the acquisition, under the Park and Recreation Land Acquisition Act, N.Y. Conserv. Law art. 16-C. The city planning commission, the city board of estimates, and the city council approved the acquisition pursuant to the Act. Various state agencies had recommended approval of the aid application that was before the state comptroller for audit and disbursement. The owners contended that their properties were not predominately open or natural and therefore did not meet the standards for acquisition pursuant to the Act because the properties were fully developed and were utilized for commercial and industrial purposes, and that acceptance for state aid was illegal, arbitrary, and capricious. The owners further contended that the city's action were void because those actions were part of the application process. The court held that the petition failed to state a cause of action as to the city officials because all of the city's actions were authorized by law.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss as to the city officials. The court denied the motion to dismiss as to the state officials. The court authorized the state officials to file their answer to the petition. The court set a hearing date as to certain allegations in the second cause of action of the property owners' petition.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Eminent domain -- Park and Recreation Land Acquisition Act -- owners of properties and businesses within area proposed to be appropriated allege that said lands are not "predominantly open or natural lands" (Conservation Law, § 881, subd. 2); petition is sufficient as to State officials and shall be set down for hearing -- but petition is dismissed as to city officials, since, even if State's three-fourths share of cost of acquisition is not forthcoming, city may still proceed and pay compensation (New York City Charter, §§ 199, 381).

1. The Park and Recreation Land Acquisition Act (Conservation Law, art. 16-C) provides that the cost of acquisition of land for park and recreation purposes under said act shall be borne three fourths by the State and one fourth by the municipality. The law further provides, in section 881 entitled "Standards for acquisition": "2. Lands acquired * * * shall consist of predominantly open or natural lands". Pursuant to said law, the City of New York has authorized the institution of condemnation proceedings to acquire 23.3 acres and 44.3 acres in Queens County. Petitioners ( CPLR, art. 78) own real property in said acreage and they claim that [***2] said acres are not "predominantly open or natural lands" but rather are fully utilized for commercial and industrial purposes. They further claim that a statement in the proceedings that there are 80 buildings on the acreage has been willfully and deceptively changed to read 14 buildings. It cannot be said that these petitioners are in the same general class as citizens and taxpayers who cannot ordinarily challenge official State acts; rather, these petitioners are owners of property and businesses which will be specifically and particularly affected by an allegedly unlawful taking. Their petition for judicial review is sufficient as to the State officials named: the State Council of Parks, the State Conservation Commissioner, and the State Comptroller. Said respondents may answer the petition and the issues will be set down for a hearing.

2. However, the petition is dismissed as to the city officials named: the Mayor and Board of Estimate and City Council and Planning Commission and Director of the Budget of the City of New York. If the city fails to obtain State funds, it may still proceed itself with the proposed condemnation for a public park use (New York City Charter, §§ [***3] 199, 381), in which event the petitioners will be awarded and paid full compensation by the city.

 

2275 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Curran v. Rouse Transp. Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


42 Misc. 2d 1055; 249 N.Y.S.2d 718; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1953



March 23, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a transportation company and its subcontractor, brought motions to set aside service of the summons and complaint in the action for wrongful death arising out of an automobile accident in Vermont on the grounds that they were improperly served under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act §§ 229, 229-b and under N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 313.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff administratrix brought a wrongful death suit after her intestate, a New York resident, was killed in an automobile accident with defendants' tractor-trailer on a Vermont highway about 15 miles from the New York border. Defendants sought dismissal of the summons and complaint, contending that New York did not have long arm jurisdiction over them. The court agreed, holding that: (1) the tractor was owned by the subcontractor who lived and was based in Vermont; (2) the trailer was owned by transportation company, which was a Vermont corporation; (3) defendants' business was to provide regular mail transportation service between New York and Vermont; (4) the death arose out of an automobile accident in Vermont and not out of any business transacted in New York; and (5) at the time of the accident the defendants were not doing or transacting any business within New York.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions and dismissed the complaint in the action for wrongful death arising out of an automobile accident in Vermont.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Process -- service on nonresidents -- personal service on alleged agent of defendants, foreign corporation and nonresidents not effective to give jurisdiction -- jurisdiction not obtained over foreign corporation and its officer by personal service without State, where neither was transacting business within State -- jurisdiction not obtained over nonresident individual, who may have been doing business within State, where cause of action based on accident in Vermont did not arise out of that business.

1. Personal service on an alleged agent of defendants, a foreign corporation and nonresident individuals, was ineffective under sections 229 and 229-b of the Civil Practice Act since the service was not made upon any of the persons described in those sections.

2. Jurisdiction was not obtained over a foreign corporation and its officer, which corporation entered into a contract with the United States to transport mail between Albany, New York and Burlington, Vermont, and then assigned the contract for performance to individual defendant, a nonresident, where the individual defendant who owned his own tractor rented the corporation's trailer and his employee was operating said [***2] tractor and trailer when it was involved in a collision in Vermont, which caused the death of plaintiff's intestate. Neither the corporation nor its officer was transacting any business in New York and personal service upon them in Vermont was ineffective.

3. As to the assignee of the mail carrying contract, jurisdiction may only be obtained over him by personal service outside the State, if the cause of action arose from the business he was doing or transacting within this State. While he may have been doing business within the State, plaintiff's cause of action, which is based upon an accident in Vermont, did not arise out of that business. Jurisdiction was not obtained over said assignee.

 

2276 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cohn v. Cazenovia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Madison County


42 Misc. 2d 218; 247 N.Y.S.2d 919; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1956



March 20, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed an action against defendants, the Town of Cazenovia (New York) and others, seeking a determination that a Town zoning ordinance, which barred the owners from using a part of their home for one or two apartments, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In 1959, the Town published a notice of a public hearing concerning the adoption of the ordinance. Several days after the public meeting, the Town Board held a meeting and two changes were made in the proposed ordinance; the ordinance was adopted. The ordinance was not then entered in the minutes of the Town Board. It was not until March 1962 that a printed copy of the ordinance was inserted next to the page containing the minutes of the meeting in which it was adopted. The inserted copy was dissimilar from the one originally adopted in that it contained an amendment adopted in 1959 and there were other differences. In declaring the ordinance void, the court ruled that there was not substantial compliance with N.Y. Town Law § 264. Section 264 required, inter alia, that every town ordinance be entered in the town board's minutes, posted on the town's bulletin board, and published in a newspaper. All of the critical publications having taken place three years after the ordinance was adopted, the court ruled that there was no substantial compliance with § 264 which, the court presumed, required a town to make such publications within a reasonable time of adoption.


OUTCOME: The court declared the ordinance void.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- Zoning Ordinance, adopted in 1959, is invalid where procedures of Town Law ( § 264) respecting Zoning Ordinances were not complied with until three years later.

 Section 264 of the Town Law provides that "Every zoning ordinance * * * shall be entered in the minutes of the town board and a copy thereof * * * shall be published once in a newspaper published in the town * * * and a copy of such ordinance * * * shall be posted on the signboard maintained by the town clerk * * * and affidavits of the publication and posting thereof shall be filed with the town clerk. Such ordinance shall take effect ten days after such publication and posting". A town Zoning Ordinance, adopted on March 5, 1959, is invalid where the Zoning Ordinance, as subsequently changed, was inserted in the minute book in 1962, where it was posted in 1962 on the Town Clerk's bulletin board, and where the affidavit of publication and the affidavit of posting were also filed in 1962. There was no substantial compliance with the provisions of section 264 of the Town Law.

 

2277 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Havemeyer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Suffolk County


42 Misc. 2d 585; 248 N.Y.S.2d 412; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1959



March 19, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executors sought review of the decision of defendant state tax commission (New York), which determined that the value of real estate in Connecticut, which was owned by a New York partnership of which the decedent was a member, was to have been included as part of the decedent's gross estate subject to New York estate tax under N.Y. Tax Law § 249-r.


OVERVIEW: The executors alleged that under Connecticut law the land was owned by the decedent and his partner as tenants in common, and that under § 249-r out-of-state real estate was expressly excluded from the gross estate of a New York decedent. The state tax commission argued that all assets of the partnership, including the land in Connecticut, must have been included in fixing the value of the decedent's interest in the partnership. The court held that it was error to have included the value of the decedent's interest in the Connecticut real estate in determining the value of the decedent's intangible interest in the partnership. The appeal was sustained and the court ordered a redetermination of the tax. The court held that the tax law excluded the value of the decedent's interest in the foreign real estate. Each partner under the law of Connecticut owned an undivided interest as tenant in common and the value of the real estate should have been excluded in determining the value of the decedent's partnership interest.


OUTCOME: The court held that the state tax commission erred when it determined that the real estate in Connecticut was to have been included in the decedent's estate subject to taxation in New York. The appeal was sustained and the court ordered a redetermination of the tax.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Taxation -- estate tax -- realty owned by New York partnership but situated out of State is no part of gross estate of New York partner -- Tax Law ( § 249-r) excludes out-of-State realty; Partnership Law ( § 12, subd. 1; § 51, subd. 2, par. [d]) has not been given extraterritorial effect -- law of Connecticut, common law, governs title to realty there acquired by decedent and son as copartners -- partners did not equitably convert realty into personalty.

1. The law of the State where real estate is situated, and not the New York Partnership Law, determines the title to such real estate owned by a New York partnership when one of the partners who is domiciled in New York dies. Our Tax Law ( § 249-r) expressly provides as to gross estates: "except real property situated * * * outside this state". Our Partnership Law ( § 12, subd. 1; § 51, subd. 2, par. [d]) provides that "All property * * * brought into the partnership * * * by purchase or otherwise * * * is partnership property" and that "On the death of a partner his right in specific partnership property vests in the surviving partner or partners". Perhaps these provisions could constitutionally be given extraterritorial [***2] effect; but the Legislature has not so provided. On the contrary, the Tax Law ( § 249-r) expressly excludes real property outside this State, and it does not provide that a partnership interest shall be considered as an intangible interest in personal property. Accordingly, in valuing a New York decedent's interest in a partnership, for New York estate tax purposes, the value of his interest in partnership realty situated in Connecticut should be excluded.

2. Decedent, who was domiciled in New York, formed an equal partnership in real estate with his son. They acquired real estate in Connecticut by deeds to decedent and his said son as "copartners in business under the firm name of" father and son. Only one portion was sold by them. Up to the time of decedent's death, Connecticut had not adopted the Uniform Partnership Law. Under Connecticut law and common law, decedent was an equal tenant in common with his son. His will bequeathed "all of my interest in the partnership * * * to my son", naming said partner. He left his residuary estate to both of his sons. The executors paid a Connecticut succession tax, on, among other assets, decedent's half interest in said Connecticut [***3] realty, which half interest was valued at $ 163,750. The rest of decedent's interest in the partnership was valued at $ 38,892.89, as shown on the partnership books and on the Federal estate tax return. But said $ 163,750 shall be excluded from decedent's gross taxable estate in New York (Tax Law, § 249-r).

3. Assuming, without deciding, that the partners could effect an equitable conversion of the Connecticult realty into personalty, the evidence does not support any finding that they did. The partnership agreement is silent as to any accountability of the surviving partner to the representative of the deceased partner for the value of the Connecticut real estate. There was no dealing in real estate as merchandise. There was only a single sale. The fact that the value of the realty was carried on the partnership books as a partnership asset is not inconsistent with the doctrine that it retained its character as real estate with title vested in the two grantees as tenants in common subject only to their partnership equities.

 

2278 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Colletti


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


42 Misc. 2d 158; 247 N.Y.S.2d 704; 1964 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1979



March 13, 1964 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for an order granting him permission to inspect the grand jury minutes upon which the indictment was found, or in the alternative, for a dismissal of the indictment based upon the grand jury minutes. The indictment charged defendant and three co-defendants with the commission of the crime of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: A written confession was taken from defendant after the police had refused to allow an attorney, retained for him by his family while he was in custody, to see or speak with him. It was for that reason that the court of appeals reversed his conviction in the first trial. Defendant claimed that an inspection of the grand jury minutes would show a legal insufficiency of evidence to convict him of the crime charged. The only evidence introduced before the grand jury implicating defendant was his written confession.
