The landscape architect is directly responsible for matters concerning the health and safety of the community, including the proper drainage of highways, industrial sites and housing.

5. Article 148 is constitutional as a valid exercise of the police power of the State.

 

2300 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rieseberg v. State


Claim Nos. 37078, 37079, 37080, 37081


Court of Claims of New York


40 Misc. 2d 676; 243 N.Y.S.2d 887; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1487



October 26, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 1959 N.Y. Laws 685-688 (the enabling acts), plaintiff claimants sought to recover damages from defendant State, alleging that the State was negligent in connection with an automobile accident. The State's attorney-general filed a motion to dismiss the claims upon the ground that the enabling acts were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: One of the claimants was driving the automobile that collided with a State National Guard truck that was towing a cannon. The other three claimants were passengers in the automobile. The accident took place approximately nine years before the enabling acts were passed. Subsequent to the passage of the enabling acts, the claimants timely filed their claims and prosecuted them with due diligence. The evidence presented at the trial on the claims revealed that the accident was proximately caused by the negligent operation of the National Guard truck and that the claimants were free of any contributory negligence. The court denied the attorney-general's motion to dismiss the claims, noting that the State could constitutionally recognize and provide redress for its liability for past obligations.


OUTCOME: The court denied the attorney-general's motion to dismiss the claims and held that the State's negligence was the proximate cause of the automobile accident.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] State -- Court of Claim -- enabling act -- at time when claims against State for negligence of members of State militia were not within jurisdiction of Court of Claims, claimants sustained injuries in accident with member of State militia; thereafter and within three years after claims arose State waived its immunity for torts committed by State militia as to torts thereafter committed; Legislature passed acts enabling claimants to make claims; motion to dismiss claims on ground that acts are unconstitutional denied -- laws waiving rights of State retrospectively are constitutional -- when section 8-a of Court of Claims Act waiving State's immunity as to militia was passed, claims of claimants were not barred; passage of section tolled Statute of Limitations -- passage of enabling acts not prohibited by Constitution (art III, § 19) -- tolling of statute continued until passage of enabling acts; enabling acts properly enacted by Legislature.

1. Claimants were injured as the result of the negligence of a New York State National Guardsman who was so operating a truck as to cause it to collide with a vehicle operated by one claimant in which the other claimants were passengers.  [***2] The accident occurred on August 19, 1950, at which time the State had not waived its sovereign immunity from liability for torts of members of the organized militia of the State. When claimants sought to recover their damages, the Court of Claims dismissed their claims on May 15, 1951 on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction of them. Section 8-a of the Court of Claims Act became effective on May 1, 1953 and waived the State's immunity for torts committed thereafter by the militia. Claimants refiled their claims pursuant to separate enabling acts passed in 1959. The State's motion to dismiss the claims on the ground that the enabling acts were private bills and unconstitutional is denied.

2. The State may constitutionally pass retrospective laws waiving or impairing its own rights, and it may impose upon itself new liabilities with respect to transactions already past. The Legislature can provide redress for the State's liability for past obligations equally with its right to waive its immunity for claims to arise in the future.

3. When section 8-a of the Court of Claims Act became effective on May 1, 1953, the Statute of Limitations had not expired as to these claims but the [***3] section gave claimants no forum in which to present them since the section applied only to torts thereafter committed. The Statute of Limitations was thus tolled.

4. Since the statutory limitation had not expired, section 19 of article III of the Constitution prohibiting the allowance of claims barred by lapse of time did not prohibit them.

5. The tolling of the statute continued until the passage of the special enabling acts under which the claims are now presented, the enabling acts giving claimants a forum. The Legislature has a right to recognize the State's moral obligation to pay a claim and to provide a forum. While the Legislature may not sanction a gift of public moneys for private purposes, it may acknowledge the justice of private claims against the State and provide for the audit and allowance of such claims and the propriety of its action is not subject to court review.

 

2301 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Anonymous v. Anonymous


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Citywide Filiation Term


40 Misc. 2d 492; 243 N.Y.S.2d 630; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1519



October 17, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother filed a N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 545 motion to extend the father's order of support of the parties' child until the child reached the age of 21 years. The father objected to the motion on the ground that the enactment of § 545 constituted an ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: The father had been ordered to pay support to his child, which was born out of wedlock, until the child reached 16 years of age. The order was issued by a criminal court in a prior filiation proceeding. On September 1, 1962, the Family Court Act became effective. Section 545 provided in part that a father was liable for the support of an infant born out of wedlock until the child attained 21 years of age and for good cause shown a longer time with no limitations. The father argued that § 545, which raised the age of support to 21 years, was an ex post facto law. He asserted because the action was a criminal proceeding his rights were fixed by the law in effect at the time of the occurrence, which was prior to the adoption of § 545. The mother's petition for extended support was granted. The court held that § 545 was not an ex post facto law. The court stated that a filiation proceeding was not readily categorized as either a civil or a criminal action; it was a creature sui generis, to which special rules applied. The ex post facto prohibition applied only to penal statutes. Section 545 was not a penal statute because paternity proceedings were not criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The mother's application to extend the order of support until the child reached 21 years of age was granted. The court also increased the father's weekly support obligation.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Courts -- Family Court's jurisdiction of paternity proceedings -- support orders made by New York City Court of Special Sessions until child's age 16 may validly and constitutionally be extended by Family Court until child's age 21.

1. All paternity proceedings pending in the New York City Court of Special Sessions, together with the court's continuing jurisdiction to modify the orders and to increase or decrease the amounts of support, were transferred on September 1, 1962 to the Family Court (L. 1962, ch. 688). Said Court of Special Sessions had had power to order support until the child's sixteenth birthday, and to continue the order until age 21 or longer for good cause shown, whereas the Family Court has power to order support until age 21, and to continue the order beyond that age for good cause shown, and likewise has continuing jurisdiction to modify its orders of support ( N. Y. City Crim. Cts. Act, §§ 72, 69, subd. 2; Family Ct. Act, §§ 451, 545). In this case, the child for whose support the father had been ordered by the Court of Special Sessions to pay $ 8 a week was still under age 16 on September 1, 1962. The Family Court, on petition of the mother after the [***2] child reached age 16, extends the order until age 21. Petitioner may, if she wishes, have a hearing as to the amount. Respondent may, if the child becomes self-supporting, apply for relief.

2. The new statute ( Family Ct. Act, § 545) is not ex post facto or oppressive, and orders thereunder are made under due process of law.

 

2302 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Lipson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


40 Misc. 2d 663; 243 N.Y.S.2d 791; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1528



October 15, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commissioner of Accounts of Nassau County, New York sought the issuance of a warrant to a sheriff commanding him to apprehend respondent deputy superintendent of highways and bring him before the Commissioner pursuant to a subpoena served on the deputy.


OVERVIEW: The deputy claimed that the Commissioner had no authority to investigate or issue subpoenas in a matter involving town government and that he was not entitled to the relief requested even if the subpoena was proper. The court held that the Commissioner was acting within the scope of his jurisdiction in issuing the subpoena directed to the deputy. Under Nassau County, N.Y. Government Law § 206, the methods, accounts, and activities of the departments and agencies of the town governments were all matters of proper concern for the executive branch of the County government. The court determined that the relief requested by the Commissioner was proper. N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 406 permitted the indefinite detention of recalcitrant witnesses until they complied with the order of the court. The sanctions under § 406 had to be obtained from the courts by the agency that sought to use compulsion.


OUTCOME: The court issued a to the sheriff commanding him to apprehend the deputy and bring him before the Commissioner pursuant to the subpoena served on the deputy.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Witnesses -- subpoena -- under provisions of section 206 of Nassau County Government Law, Commissioner of Accounts has authority to investigate affairs of town and to issue subpoena to town official -- petitioner is entitled to issuance of warrant to Sheriff directing him to apprehend town official and bring him before Commissioner in accordance with subpoena.

1. Under the specific provisions of section 206 of the Nassau County Government Law, the Commissioner of Accounts of Nassau County has authority to investigate or issue subpoenas with respect to each officer or agency of the county "and of the towns" in Nassau County. Such grant of power is limited by the section and as the section appears in the "Executive" article of the charter, it is a grant of executive power. Petitioner was acting within the scope of his jurisdiction in issuing a subpoena to respondent, a town deputy superintendent of highways.

2. Petitioner is entitled to the issuance of a warrant to the Sheriff directing him to apprehend respondent, and bring him before petitioner under section 406 of the Civil Practice Act (now CPLR, § 2308, subd. [b]), despite section 2213 of the Nassau County Government [***2] Law which provides that disobedience to a subpoena issued by the Commissioner of Accounts is a misdemeanor. The sections are not mutually exclusive.

 

2303 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Johnson v. Denna


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 717; 243 N.Y.S.2d 797; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1549



October 10, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The writ is dismissed on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner was placed on parole following his conviction for a state charge. His parole was revoked when he was arrested on a federal charge. The prisoner commenced a habeas corpus proceeding seeking to be released from custody after his parole was revoked.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner commenced a habeas corpus proceeding alleging that his release on bail posted for the federal charge granted him a vested right to be free which was infringed by state parole officers and that his retaking and confinement infringed on his constitutional right against double jeopardy. The court dismissed the prisoner's writ, holding that the parole officers properly revoked the prisoner's privilege of parole when he was arrested on the federal charge. The court noted that the prisoner presented no evidence regarding the illegality of his federal arrest. The court found that whether the federal arrest was based on an illegal search and seizure was not relevant because the parole officers did not rely on the arrest to convict the prisoner of a crime. The court determined that the prisoner remained within the legal custody of respondent warden while he was on parole pursuant to N.Y. Correct. Law § 213. The court noted that parole was a privilege accorded to the prisoner and that it could have been withdrawn within the absolute and unreviewable discretion of the Parole Board.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


HEADNOTES

Pardon -- parole -- parole officer, upon relator's arrest for Federal charge, revoked parole; Correction Law ( § 216) under which parole officer acted, not unconstitutional -- Federal arrest not illegal; no constitutional right of relator's was violated by Parole Board.

1. When relator, a parolee, was arrested on a Federal charge while on parole, the rescission of his parole, a privilege and not a right, by his parole officer acting under section 216 of the Correction Law did not violate any of relator's constitutional rights. Section 216 is not unconstitutional and is not unconstitutional in its application to relator. The arrest of the parolee, while he enjoyed the privilege of going outside the prison walls, was ample basis for the action of the parole officer. That no Parole Board issued the warrant for his retaking making it retroactive to the date of his retaking is unconsequential.

2. The Federal arrest was not illegal. Whether the Federal arrest was or was not bottomed upon an illegal search and seizure is of no moment in this proceeding. For the information of that arrest imparted to the parole officers was not used or [***2] to be used by them to convict him of a crime, but merely to recall a privilege. No constitutional right of the petitioner was invaded by the action of the Parole Board.

 

2304 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Levine v. Oyster Bay


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


40 Misc. 2d 605; 243 N.Y.S.2d 656; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1554



October 9, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Any slight delay that may be encountered because of the intervention is outweighed by the adverse effect that would result if intervention were denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A proposed intervenor sought an order permitting it to join the action as a party plaintiff, pursuant to the provisions of N.Y. C.P.L.R. 1012, 1013.


OVERVIEW: In a resolution defendant, the Town Board of the Town of Oyster Bay, amended the town's building zone ordinance, changing the zoning classification and use of a 15-acre parcel of land owned by the individual defendants from "Residence D" to "Industrial H." The plaintiffs in the action were four residents who owned property either adjacent to or in the immediate vicinity of the land. The proposed intervenor was a contract vendee of the parcel in question, having agreed to purchase it from defendants on condition, among others, that a rezoning to "Industrial H" be obtained. Soon after the action was commenced a temporary injunction was granted restraining defendants from enforcing the zoning change pending the outcome of the action. The court held that the intervenor did have a direct and pecuniary interest in the outcome sufficient to be joined as a party plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court found that the intervenor had a direct and pecuniary interest in the outcome.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- intervention -- contract vendee of rezoned property has right to intervene in action by neighboring property owners to declare rezoning void -- motion to intervene is timely.

1. In an action by neighbors to declare void the rezoning of a parcel of land from residential to industrial, the contract vendee of the rezoned parcel, who sought to rescind the contract on the ground that the rezoning condition of the contract was not fulfilled but was opposed by the owner, has a right to intervene in the action. It has interests which will be affected by the outcome of the action and may be bound by the judgment within the meaning of section 1012 of the Civil Practice Law and Rules. Although the contract vendee will by intervention seek to invalidate the rezoning which it sought, since, in approving the change, the town imposed conditions which the contract vendee alleges may create additional obstacles and necessitate further delays in the use of property, such consideration is outweighed.

2. The words "timely motion"  [***2] to intervene in section 1012 of the Civil Practice Law and Rules mean within a reasonable time, and here it was timely after the contract vendee had definite knowledge that the owner had rejected its request for rescission.

 

2305 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Asso. of Private Day Schools, Inc. v. Baumgartner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


41 Misc. 2d 560; 245 N.Y.S.2d 733; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1576



October 3, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the defendants' motion for judgment is granted and plaintiffs' cross motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant members of the Board of Health of the City of New York filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings dismissing plaintiff association's amended complaint, and the association filed a cross motion for dismissal of the board's amended answer. The association's action sought to declare unconstitutional sections of New York City, N.Y., Health Code art. 47 that regulated day care services and to restrain the enforcement thereof.


OVERVIEW: The association alleged that the challenged regulations unconstitutionally usurped legislative functions beyond the board's jurisdiction of the board, that they discriminated against private institutions, and that they were vague, illusory, and did not define their standards. The court granted the board's motion and denied the association's cross motion, holding that its constitutional attack was groundless. The challenged regulations did not conflict with regulations issued by the state department of education, with which compliance was voluntary. The board was authorized to promulgate regulations to protect and promote public health and had the power to enact local code provisions additional to state enactments. The provisions came within both the scope of the police power and the protection of the presumption of constitutionality. The regulations were enforceable against both public and private institutions and did not discriminate unconstitutionally against private day care services. Although the association's schools complied with previous regulations, the new regulations did not become unconstitutional because they imposed new financial burdens upon association members.


OUTCOME: The court granted the board's motion for judgment on the pleadings dismissing the association's amended complaint seeking to declare sections of the New York City, N.Y. Health Code to be unconstitutional. The court denied the association's cross motion for dismissal of the board's amended answer.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- regulation of private nursery schools and kindergartens -- New York City Health Code requirements for permits to operate private "Day Care Services" are valid exercise of police power, and do not encroach upon regulations of city Board of Education or of State Department of Education or upon State Sanitary Code or Rules of State Board of Social Welfare.

Acting under the New York City Charter (§ 558), the New York City Board of Health has revised and repealed much of the old Sanitary Code of the City of New York and has enacted a new and modernized New York City Health Code. Article 47 of said Health Code, entitled "Day Care Services", is authorized by the police power of the State through its municipality, the city, and is presumed to be constitutional unless shown to have no reasonable relation to the public health or welfare. It is not unconstitutional merely because it imposes new financial burdens on proprietors of existing nursery schools and kindergartens. Specifically, section 47.05 (subd. [a], par. [5]) requiring an applicant for a permit [***2] to conduct a day care service to furnish "Evidence of a reasonably secure financial position to permit compliance with the provisions of this Code", and section 47.07 (subd. [a], par. [1]) fixing a minimum age of two years for a child to be admitted to a day care service, and section 47.13 (subds. [a], [b]) requiring a minimum floor area of 30 square feet for each child, and sections 47.09 (subds. [a], [b], [d], [e]) and 47.11 (subds. [a], [b], [d]) setting forth the qualifications required for the teachers and staff and the conditions of supervision, are unambiguous, valid and constitutional. They do not abrogate or encroach upon the regulations of the New York City Board of Education and of the State Department of Education, or upon the State Sanitary Code or the Rules of the State Board of Social Welfare (cf. Social Welfare Law, § 390). The State has not completely pre-empted the field. The above-cited regulations of the New York City Health Code are in accord with modern public health practices, and this action for a judgment declaring them unconstitutional is dismissed.

 

2306 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Schacht v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 303; 243 N.Y.S.2d 272; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1600



September 27, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions, plaintiff laundromat owners sought a declaratory judgment that New York City, N.Y., Local Law No. 14 (1961) was invalid and unconstitutional, and injunctive relief. On interlocutory appeal, a temporary injunction that enjoined the enforcement of the Sunday closing provision, was modified so as to strike out a decretal paragraph, which amounted to a final determination. As modified the order was affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Local Law No. 14 amended New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ B32-167.0, B32-173.0 so as to require licenses for automatic and coin-operated laundry operations and regulate business hours. The owners' actions for declaratory judgment were consolidated. The court declared that the local law was valid as to weekdays and as requiring laundry operations to remain closed from midnight to 6:00 a.m. on Sundays. However, the law was invalid as to requiring closing or an attendant on Sundays from 6:00 a.m. to midnight. The court enjoined the enforcement of the invalid portions of the law. The basic issue was the validity of the local law under the due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions, the home rule provisions of the state constitution, and the city home rule law. The court found that the state had pre-empted the field of Sunday legislation. The court concluded that the regulation of the evening hours was a proper municipal function taking reasonable steps toward the control and reduction of crime, during the midnight to 6:00 a.m. hours. There was no reason why the daytime Sunday hours, which were not otherwise prohibited by state law, should have been restricted.


OUTCOME: The court entered a declaratory judgment that in part invalidated the local law that regulated weekday and Sunday business hours of automatic and coin-operated laundry operations. The court enjoined the enforcement of the invalid portions of the local law.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- local law regulating laundromats -- local law validly requires laundromats to have attendant from 6:00 P.M. to midnight on weekdays and to be closed from midnight to 6:00 A.M. on weekdays and Sundays; invalid insofar as it requires closing after 6:00 A.M. on Sundays, and insofar as it requires attendant on any part of Sunday -- Legislature has pre-empted these Sabbath subjects -- excision of part and retention of part do not depend so much on sentence structure as on legislative intent.

1. The Administrative Code of the City of New York (§ B32-173.0, subds. f, g, as amd. by Local Laws, 1961, No. 14 of City of New York) provides in part: "f. All laundry operations, whether automatic or coin operated, whether attended or unattended, shall close all day Sunday and between the hours of 12:00 midnight to 6:00 A.M. on all other days. g. All coin operated laundries shall be required to have on the premises an attendant from 6:00 p.m. until closing." This regulation is reasonable, constitutional and valid (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 12; General City Law, § 20, subd. 13; New York City Charter, § 27, subd. a) insofar as it requires an attendant from 6:00 [***2] p.m. to midnight on weekdays, and insofar as it requires closing from midnight to 6:00 a.m. on weekdays and on Sundays. This regulation is invalid insofar as it requires closing on Sundays after 6:00 a.m., and insofar as it might be construed to require an attendant on any part of a Sunday, since the State Legislature has pre-empted these Sabbath subjects (Penal Law, art. 192).

2. The severability of the invalid portions of a law, and the question of which of the valid portions shall be retained, turn not so much on the sentence structure and paragraph arrangement, as on the presumed or indicated legislative intent in case of such partial invalidity.

 

2307 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Epps


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 661; 243 N.Y.S.2d 833; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1602



September 27, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The application herein is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion for the right to be tried before a jury under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 32. The State charged each defendant with a misdemeanor offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' motion was based solely on the contention that there was a possibility that in the three-judge trial, which was provided for misdemeanor offenses pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 40, a nonunanimous determination was permitted, which was unconstitutional. The court disagreed and found that the case law relied upon by defendants was dicta. The court found that defendants sought a jury trial without regard to the nature or type of misdemeanor charged, based on the possibility that there might not be a unanimous determination. The court found that if it granted defendants' request, all defendants charged with misdemeanors could make a like application on such a ground. The court further held that even assuming that the provision for a determination by two of the three-judge panel was held unconstitutional, the remedy existed in some change in that provision and not in a wholesale granting of jury trials for misdemeanors.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' application.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- prosecution by indictment -- motion of defendants, charged with misdemeanors in New York City Criminal Court that charges be prosecuted by indictment, in absence of showing of special circumstances, is denied; claim that determination by two of three-Judge court is unconstitutional not here involved.

A motion of defendants, charged with misdemeanors and an offense in the New York City Criminal Court, that the Supreme Court certify that it is reasonable that the charges be prosecuted by indictment with the right to a jury trial is denied where defendants have shown no special circumstances warranting such relief other than their claim that, if they are tried by a three-Judge court without a jury, a determination of guilt by two of the three Judges is unconstitutional. Nonjury trials by three-Judge panels is authorized by the Constitution. The question of the constitutionality of that provision is not here involved.

 

2308 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Harriman v. Kabinoff


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Orange County


40 Misc. 2d 387; 243 N.Y.S.2d 210; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1611



September 25, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village brought an action against defendants, an owner of a mobile home park and a lessee, to enjoin defendants' continued maintenance of the mobile home park without application for and issuance of a permit as required by an ordinance. The village requested a temporary injunction, and defendant filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The village adopted an ordinance which provided that automobile trailers could only be maintained within the village if a permit was obtained by a majority vote from a board of trustees. The village brought an action against defendants for the failure to apply for the permits. The village filed a motion for a temporary injunction, and defendants filed a cross-motion for summary judgment claiming that the ordinance was unconstitutional. Defendants agreed that they would not permit any additional mobile homes upon their premises until the matter was resolved. The court granted summary judgment for the village pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212(b). The court held that under N.Y. Village Law § 89(59) the village was permitted to enact the ordinance for the promotion of the public welfare. The regulation of trailer camps bore a substantial relation to the public welfare and was a valid exercise of the police power. The regulation of trailer camps, relating to the public welfare, was an exercise of a legislative function and no general standards had to be formulated. The court ruled that mobile home parks were included in the ordinance even though only automobile trailers was mentioned.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to the village.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- regulation of house trailer camps -- villages had "welfare" power to regulate trailer camps, even before expressly empowered -- "mobile homes" are "automobile trailers" -- ordinance vesting permit power in village's own board of trustees need not define standards for permits.

1. Even before villages were expressly empowered to regulate "house trailer camps", they had such power under their general "welfare" power (Village Law, § 89, subds. 59, 69). An ordinance prohibiting "automobile trailers" unless a special permit were applied for and issued upon a majority vote of the village's board of trustees and on such conditions as might be imposed by the board for the welfare of the village, constitutionally and validly applies to a so-called "mobile homes" development.

2. Such an ordinance, vesting the permit power in the legislative body itself, need not define the standards required for issuing permits.

 

2309 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sullivan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Oneida County


40 Misc. 2d 278; 242 N.Y.S.2d 988; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1623



September 18, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to vacate the search warrants and to suppress the evidence seized thereby is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to vacate search warrants issued and to suppress the evidence obtained by the State as a result of the execution of the search warrants. Defendants claimed that the affidavits on which the search warrants were based were legally insufficient and contained no factual information sufficient to indicate probable cause for the issuance of the search warrants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants filed a motion to vacate search warrants issued and to suppress the evidence obtained by the State as a result of the execution of the search warrants. Defendants claimed that the affidavits on which the search warrants were based were legally insufficient and contained no factual information sufficient to indicate probable cause for the issuance of the search warrants. Defendants also argued that the affidavits did not indicate any probable cause supported by facts and circumstances therein to indicate that any law was being violated. The court rejected defendants' arguments. The court noted that probable cause existed when there was reasonable ground of suspicion supported by facts and circumstances strong enough to warrant a cautious man in the belief that the law was being violated on the premises to be searched. Here, the court determined that the decision to issue the search warrants was neither arbitrary nor patently erroneous. The court also found that the fact that the facts underlying the search warrants were sworn to before a different judge than the one that signed the search warrants was not unduly prejudicial and sufficiently complied with the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to vacate the search warrants and to suppress the evidence.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- probable cause for search warrant and seizure of contraband was shown by affidavits as to intercepted telephone calls giving United States Treasury balance numbers -- affidavits verified before Magistrate who issued warrant of arrest were properly submitted three days later to Justice who thereupon properly issued search warrant without personally examining affiants (cf. Code Crim. Pro., § 794).

1. Policy slips, lottery tickets, and records of book-making plays are contraband, the mere possession of which constitutes a public offense. This motion to vacate search warrants and to suppress contraband seized thereunder is denied. Probable cause was shown by statements in the affidavits in support of the search warrants that, pursuant to court orders, the affiants intercepted telephone conversations between the defendants and heard them give numbers which were the same as the daily published United States Treasury balance numbers.

2. The Code of Criminal Procedure ( § 794) states that the person seeking a search warrant [***2] "shall appear personally before the judge, * * * who may * * * examine, on oath * * * and must take the affidavit". Here, affidavits in support of warrants of arrest for alleged violations of section 1372 of the Penal Law were verified before a City Court Judge or Magistrate, and, three days later, those affidavits were submitted to a Justice of the Supreme Court, who thereupon issued these search warrants. It was within the discretion of said Justice whether or not to examine the affiants personally. This motion in the County Court to vacate the search warrants is denied.

 

2310 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Chusud Realty Corp. v. Kensington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Nassau County


40 Misc. 2d 259; 243 N.Y.S.2d 149; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1631



September 16, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant municipality to declare the municipality's zoning of a parcel of land purchased by the property owner unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that the municipality's zoning of the property was unconstitutional. The municipality argued that the property owner brought the property with knowledge of its zoning and with the intention of making a profit and therefore was precluded from testing the validity of the municipality's ordinance. The court rejected the municipality's argument, finding that the payment of a premium purchase price for property did not disqualify the property owner from arguing that the property's zoning was unconstitutional in relation to the fair market value of the property. The municipality also argued that testimony as to the economic loss suffered if the property zoning were not changed. The court accepted this argument, finding that testimony as to the value of the property considering a change in zoning was inadmissible. Ultimately, the court found that the municipality's ordinance went too far in the name of aesthetics and caused hardship to the property owner.


OUTCOME: The court granted judgment to the property owner and determined that the present zoning of its property arbitrary and unreasonable.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- one-family zoning ordinance, which has remained unchanged for over 30 years as to plaintiff's property on principal thoroughfare on which all else is zoned for commercial or apartment house use, is adjudged unconstitutional and void as to plaintiff's property.

A village zoning ordinance restricts plaintiff's property to use for one-family dwellings and accessory use as professional office, and to use for schools and public buildings. The ordinance has remained thus unchanged as to plaintiff's property for over 30 years, even though this property is on a principal thoroughfare on which all other properties for two and one-half miles are now zoned for commercial or apartment house uses, and even though the last time a one-family residence was built in this area was 39 years ago. There is no demand for plaintiff's property for school or public building use; and the court is satisfied that, even considering possible professional accessory use, the influence of the surrounding entirely commercial and apartment house area would make impossible the sale of residences along this thoroughfare at a price compatible with the applicable tax rates,  [***2] even if this property were to be subdivided. A village's zoning of land on a principal thoroughfare cannot ignore the zoning outside the village's borders. This zoning precludes any use for which plaintiff's property is reasonably adapted. As to plaintiff's property, the ordinance is adjudged to be arbitrary, unreasonable, unconstitutional and void. Of course, it remains for the Village Board to determine what is "the most appropriate use of land" (Village Law, § 177).

 

2311 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Udell v. McFadyen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial and Special Term, Nassau County


40 Misc. 2d 265; 243 N.Y.S.2d 156; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1632



September 16, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court rendered its decision on a complaint filed by a landowner, which sought the invalidation of an ordinance by which defendant village board rezoned property from business to residential uses. The landowner claimed that the ordinance was invalid because it was not in accordance with a master plan, was discriminatory, and was confiscatory.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned two parcels of land within the village. One of the parcels was adjacent to property that was used for retail and other business purposes. The second parcel was adjacent to a nursery school and a gas station. The parcels were zoned for business use when the landowner acquired them, but the village board adopted an ordinance to rezone the land for residential use. The court held that the ordinance was in accordance with a comprehensive plan because it conformed to the village's master plan and because it was consistent and based upon the need to control traffic congestion. The court determined that the reduction of the property values after it was rezoned was not conclusive on the issue of whether the ordinance was confiscatory. Because the value of the first parcel was reduced, the parcel was rendered useless by the rezoning, and there were existing business uses in the area that was rezoned, the court determined that the ordinance was unconstitutional as to that parcel.


OUTCOME: The court invalidated the rezoning ordinance as to one of the parcels owner by the landowner.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- shape, terrain and surroundings of plaintiff's parcel are such that reclassification from business zone to residential zone would preclude any reasonably adaptable use; moreover, zoning amendment unreasonably discriminates against plaintiff's parcel by failing similarly to reclassify similarly circumstanced retail services area in this same business zone; therefore, amendment is unconstitutional and void as to plaintiff's parcel -- but, as to another parcel owned by plaintiff on other side of same thoroughfare, amendment is valid -- substantial reduction in value does not constitute confiscation.

Two business zones in a village were reclassified as a residential zone, except for a small portion. The zoning ordinance amendment was "made in accordance with a comprehensive plan" and "designed to lessen congestion in the streets" and "to facilitate the adequate provision of transportation" (Village Law, § 177). Plaintiff property owner's investment in one parcel thus reclassified was $ 160,000, and its value if zoned for business was $ 425,000 while its value if zoned as residential is only $ 165,000; and his investment in another parcel thus [***2] reclassified was $ 65,000, and its value if zoned for business was $ 250,000 while its value if zoned as residential is only $ 46,000; but these figures do not constitute confiscation. However, as to the latter, which is a vacant parcel on the other side of the same main thoroughfare, (1) plaintiff has sustained the burden of proving that its shape and terrain and surroundings are such that the residential reclassification would preclude any use of this parcel to which it is reasonably adaptable, and (2) plaintiff has proved that this amendment discriminates against his parcel without reasonable basis and therefore denies him the equal protection of the law, by its failure to include in this residential reclassification an area which is adjacent to his and which is circumstanced the same as his except that it contains some retail stores and businesses which would still remain in the business zone and which would therefore have the right to change to any other use permissible in a business zone; accordingly, the rezoning amendment is declared unconstitutional and void as to this parcel of plaintiff's.

 

2312 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Birch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


40 Misc. 2d 626; 243 N.Y.S.2d 525; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1662



September 6, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] It follows, therefore, that the indictment must be and it is hereby dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to dismiss an indictment that charged them, in eight counts, with violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141 and with conspiracy to violate § 1141, in that they did sell and distribute eight books of an obscene nature.


OVERVIEW: The books contained lurid descriptions of sexual activities, both hetero and homosexual. No socially unacceptable language was used. Although the books were "trash" and had no literary value, they were not obscene. In so ruling, the court stated that the books did not go beyond the compromise between candor and shame at which the community had arrived. Rather, they were within the mores of the times and did not constitute hard-core pornography.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- obscenity -- eight books, involved in indictment charging defendants with violation of section 1141 of Penal Law, are not hard-core pornography and are not obscene; indictment dismissed.

The eight books involved in an indictment charging defendants with conspiracy to violate section 1141 of the Penal Law, in that they sold and distributed such books, are filled with lurid descriptions of sexual activities in sufficient detail to act as an erotic stimulus to those so inclined. They avoid socially unacceptable language. Such books, in the mores of these days, do not constitute hard-core pornography though they are coarse. They are not obscene within the meaning of section 1141 of the Penal Law, as that section must be constitutionally construed in light of the free press guarantee of the First Amendment and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the Constitution. The indictment is dismissed.

 

2313 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Crane v. Prudential Ins. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Westchester County


40 Misc. 2d 480; 243 N.Y.S.2d 514; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1674



September 4, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The order appealed from is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigant sought review of an order entered in the Police Justice Court of the Village of Port Chester (New York) that granted defendant foreign corporation's motion to vacate service of a summons and to dismiss the action on the ground that the court did not have jurisdiction over the foreign corporation.


OVERVIEW: The litigant filed an action to recover a sum of money from the foreign corporation. The lower court dismissed the action on the basis that it had no jurisdiction over the foreign corporation. On appeal, the litigant argued that jurisdiction existed over the foreign corporation because it was an insurance corporation doing business within the state on whom service of process could be effected by service on a local or general agent residing in the county pursuant to N.Y. Jud. Law § 54. The foreign corporation argued that service on it was void as it contravened N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 18 because as a foreign corporation, it was not amenable to jurisdiction in the county court on which the lower court's jurisdiction was predicated. The court agreed with the foreign corporation. The court noted that as an inferior local court, the lower court's jurisdiction was limited by the jurisdiction conferred by the legislature on the county courts. In this case, as the legislature had not conferred jurisdiction over foreign corporations in the county courts, the lower court here had no jurisdiction over the foreign corporation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court.


HEADNOTES

Corporations -- foreign corporations -- foreign corporation not amenable to jurisdiction of Justice Court.

Justice's Courts cannot have "greater jurisdiction * * * than is conferred upon county courts" (N. Y. Const., former art. VI, § 18). The County Courts have not been given jurisdiction of foreign corporations, even when the corporation does business in this State and has its principal place of business in that county (Civ. Prac. Act, § 67, subd. 3; § 68). Therefore, the Justice Court Act (§§ 10, 51, 54) and the Port Chester Police Justice Court Act (L. 1949, ch. 851, § 13) cannot constitutionally confer such jurisdiction on such inferior courts. Accordingly, in this action in the Police Justice Court of the Village of Port Chester, Westchester County, for $ 41.25, against a New Jersey insurance corporation which is authorized to do business in New York State and which has an office in the City of White Plains, Westchester County, the service of summons in White Plains on the manager of said office was vacated.

 

2314 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Benway


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Justices' Court of New York, Town of Kingsbury, County of Washington


41 Misc. 2d 39; 244 N.Y.S.2d 163; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1691



August 23, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The charge against the defendant is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1180, subd. (a), driving at a speed greater than reasonable and prudent under the existing conditions. The charge resulted from an accident involving defendant's vehicle and another vehicle after defendant's vehicle skidded on a dirt road.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's vehicle skidded about 30 feet on a secondary dirt road, defendant's vehicle and another vehicle sideswiped each other at a slight bend in the road. At defendant's trial for driving at a speed greater than reasonable and prudent under the existing conditions, there was no actual testimony as to the speed of defendant's vehicle. The only substantial proof presented was first, that an accident occurred, and second, that defendant's vehicle skidded. The mere fact that defendant was driving at such a speed as to skid in the ordinary course of driving was not enough to convict him. Therefore, the testimony presented did not prove a prima facie case against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the charge against defendant.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- speeding -- proof that defendant skidded and that accident occurred is insufficient to establish defendant's guilt of speeding in violation of Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 1180, subd. [a]).

The People failed to prove that defendant was guilty of speeding in violation of subdivision (a) of section 1180 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law in that he drove his vehicle at a speed "greater than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions and having regard to the actual and potential hazards then existing" by proof that defendant skidded and that an accident occurred.

 

2315 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Ronny


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Juvenile Term, Queens County


40 Misc. 2d 194; 242 N.Y.S.2d 844; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1693



August 23, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile was before the court in a fact-finding hearing pursuant to a petition by petitioner correction officer to determine delinquency pursuant to N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 716(a), which was a hearing to determine whether the juvenile did the act or acts alleged in the petition which, if done by an adult, would have constituted a crime.


OVERVIEW: In a petition to determine delinquency, a juvenile was charged with unlawfully possessing barbiturates and Doriden. He confessed to the correction officer that they were drugs and consented to being searched. In the finding of fact hearing to determine delinquency, the court held that: (1) the pills in the juvenile's possession were "drugs or devices" whose possession, sale, and/or distribution by the juvenile were unlawful; and (2) no additional corroboration of the juvenile's extrajudicial confession was required because additional corroboration was found in the form of the officer himself who had observed the juvenile's intoxicated appearance while committing the elements of the crime of sale and distribution, and because the pills themselves were entered into evidence. The court also denied the motion to suppress evidence found on the juvenile by the officer because the search and seizure were not "unreasonable" because a "peace officer", pursuant to N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. § 154-a (1963), could make a warrantless arrest if a non-felony crime was being committed or attempted in his presence.


OUTCOME: The court found that the correction officer had proven his prima facie case that the juvenile had unlawfully possessed and distributed drugs. The court ruled that the juvenile had the burden at the next hearing to go forward with defense evidence and if not successful, the finding would stand with finality.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Infants -- delinquent child -- 15-year-old boy was seen to effect sale of pills, surrendered by him to officer, to another; pills were drugs and sale was illegal -- on petition to determine that respondent was delinquent, requirement of Family Court Act ( § 744) that confession of boy be corroborated was met by circumstantial evidence -- respondent's possession and sale of drugs was misdemeanor if committed by older person and delinquency petition was supported -- amendment of petition to eliminate reference to "Doriden" as barbiturate was ordered -- where respondent consented to be frisked, voluntarily emptied pockets of vials of pills and voluntarily confessed, officer had reasonable ground for search and subsequent arrest; motion to suppress was denied.

1. A correction officer observed respondent, a 15-year-old boy, take a dollar placed on a mail box by a youth, and pass to the youth something in his hand. After respondent walked away unsteadily the officer approached and spoke to respondent. The officer identified himself and asked that respondent permit him to frisk respondent. Respondent agreed and later emptied his pockets of two unlabeled bottles containing pills [***2] and nine one-dollar bills. Respondent confessed that the white pills were "Doriden" and the green pills were barbiturates, which he sold for stated prices. Respondent confessed that he had been taking them and that his "doped" condition resulted from taking some. The pills in evidence were drugs and the sale of some of them to the youth was an unlawful sale.

2. On this petition to determine whether respondent was delinquent, competent evidence was required by section 744 of the Family Court Act and such section also provided that an uncorroborated confession made out of court was insufficient. In this case, respondent's confession was corroborated by evidence of the drugged physical appearance and shuffling gait of respondent, by the pills, by the nine one-dollar bills, by respondent's identification of the pills as "Doriden" and "barbiturates" which respondent knew were drugs because of the effects on his own body. Chemical analysis of the pills was therefore unnecessary.

3. Respondent's possession and sale of barbiturates and "Doriden", a drug, would have violated section 1740, and section 1747-b (possession of barbiturate without a proper label) of the Penal Law, a misdemeanor [***3] if committed by an older person and therefore supported the delinquency petition and a finding of delinquency. Respondent, however, was granted an opportunity to go forward with defense evidence.

4. Amendment of the petition was granted to eliminate a reference to "Doriden" as a barbiturate.

5. The arresting officer frisked respondent with respondent's consent and respondent voluntarily emptied his pockets of the vials of pills and voluntarily confessed. When the vials and confession were disclosed, a misdemeanor of unlawfully possessing unlabeled narcotics was disclosed to the arresting officer and the search and seizure were reasonable and the officer had power to arrest even without a warrant. Respondent's motion to suppress evidence was denied.

 

2316 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Burton v. Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


40 Misc. 2d 50; 242 N.Y.S.2d 510; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1719



August 12, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow initiated a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 for an order directing respondents, the city and the Board of Trustees of the Police Pension Fund of Albany (New York), to add her name to its pension rolls for an annual pension payment retrospectively to the date of death of her decedent husband, a retired police officer. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss the widow's petition.


OVERVIEW: The widow applied for a court order directing respondents to pay her an annual pension payment from the date of her decedent husband's death. Respondents filed a responsive motion to dismiss the widow's application, contending that the widow's petition did not state sufficient facts to substantiate her claim for the relief sought, that the court lacked jurisdiction to grant the petitioned relief, and that the widow's application was not timely filed. The court denied the widow's application based on its determination that the statutory amendment providing for a widow's pension was prospective, rather than retrospective, in operation and did not apply to include the widow whose husband had retired approximately six years prior to the relevant amendment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the widow's petition.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- pensions -- petition of widow of retired member of Police Department of City of Albany to compel payment of $ 900 pension to her was dismissed -- Local Law No. 1 of 1952 authorizing such pension payment to widows was then unconstitutional; moreover, Local Law did not apply to petitioner's husband who retired in 1946; Local Law was prospective -- amendment of Constitution, effective January 1, 1960, to permit municipalities to grant pensions to widows did not refer to 1952 Local Law and did not validate such law; moreover, amendment was also prospective.

1. The petition of a widow of a retired member of the Police Department of the City of Albany for an order directing the trustees of the Police Pension Fund of said city to place her name on its pension rolls and pay her $ 900 yearly was dismissed.

2. Petitioner's husband retired in 1946 and was paid a pension until he died in 1962. Under Local Law No. 1 of 1940 of said city effective at his retirement, only the husband was entitled to a pension. By Local Law No. 1 of 1952 these local laws were amended so as to grant to a widow of a retired policeman after his death the sum [***2] of $ 900 per year. In 1952 section 1 of article VIII of the State Constitution provided that no municipality give money to any individual. Section 8 of article VII of the Constitution, as amended effective January 1, 1952, provided that the Legislature might increase the amount of a pension. Chapter 319 of the Laws of 1952 empowered any municipality to adopt and amend a local law providing for supplemental pension payments to retired employees. Section 1 of article VIII of the Constitution, as amended effective January 1, 1960, granted power to a municipality to increase the pension benefits to retired members of a police department or to widows of retired members of a police department. The constitutional provisions in effect when Local Law No. 1 of 1952 was adopted prohibited an increase in pension benefits to petitioner's husband in the form of a pension for his widow. Moreover, Local Law No. 1 of 1952 was prospective in application and not retrospective to a person who had retired in 1946.

3. The amendment to section 1 of article VIII of the Constitution, effective January 1, 1960, did not validate the Local Law of 1952. The unconstitutional Local Law was not expressly [***3] or impliedly ratified and confirmed therein. Moreover, said amendment was also prospective in operation.

 

2317 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Scifo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 110; 242 N.Y.S.2d 980; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1730



August 7, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to set aside his convictions of violations of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 1140, 483.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after trial of violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 1140 and 483. The case was tried before a panel of three judges and one of the judges dissented and voted to acquit. Defendant moved to set aside the conviction and for arrest of judgment on the ground that the conviction by two out of three judges violated the defendant's constitutional rights. Defendant argued that the fact that one of the judges voted to acquit his guilt was not established beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that while defendant was entitled to the benefit of every reasonable doubt on the facts, the State was entitled to any reasonable doubt a trial judge may have had upon the law for. The court found that a dissenting vote based upon a doubt as to the law did not establish reasonable doubt as to defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- conviction by two of three Judges in nonjury trial -- question of constitutionality of conviction by two of three Judges in nonjury trial was left for determination by higher court.

The question of whether a defendant, tried by a three-Judge court without a jury in the Criminal Court of the City of New York, was convicted by two out of the three Judges -- the third Judge having a reasonable doubt -- in violation of his constitutional rights to have his guilt proven beyond a reasonable doubt, was one of constitutional law which was left for determination to a higher court. Defendant's motion to set aside the conviction was denied.

 

2318 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Dessner v. MJR Realty Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


40 Misc. 2d 229; 242 N.Y.S.2d 690; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1752



July 30, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the court denies the motion for summary judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fireman filed an action against defendant citizen for damages related to injuries the fireman suffered in response to a fire at the citizen's premises. The fireman filed a motion for summary judgment pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 205-a.


OVERVIEW: The fireman alleged that he was severely injured while fighting a fire in the citizen's building. He further alleged that 90 days prior to the fire the citizen had received a notice from the city building department that the building was in a dilapidated condition so as to be dangerous to the life and safety of others. The notice directed the citizen to demolish the building. The fireman sought summary judgment under § 205-a, which provided that a person whose violation of a code or statute resulted in injury to a fireman was liable for payment of a certain sum to the fireman. The citizen alleged that the statute was unconstitutional and that he did not receive the violation notice. The court held that the statute did not deny any class of individuals equal protection of the laws and that it was constitutional. The fireman's summary judgment motion was denied, however, because the citizen had raised an issue of fact regarding notice of the violation.


OUTCOME: The court denied the fireman's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Negligence -- injuries to fireman -- in action under General Municipal Law ( § 205-a) by fireman injured while fighting fire in building on which violation had been served, motion for summary judgment was denied where issue of fact as to service of notice of violation on defendant existed -- section 205-a of General Municipal Law was constitutional.

1. In an action by a fireman to recover under section 205-a of the General Municipal Law because he was injured while fighting a fire in a building upon which a violation had been served by the Building Department of a city, plaintiff's motion for summary judgment was denied since an issue of fact existed as to whether a notice of violation had in fact been served on defendant.

2. Section 205-a of the General Municipal Law was constitutional and did not deny equal protection of the laws since all persons in the same class were treated alike.

 

2319 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Whitmier & Ferris Co. v. New York State Thruway Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


39 Misc. 2d 919; 242 N.Y.S.2d 386; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1803



July 15, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The plaintiff's motion for an injunction pendente lite is denied, the temporary injunction granted in the show cause order and continued on the argument of the motion is vacated and the defendant's cross motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that the court has no jurisdiction over the subject of the action is granted, all without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff advertising company brought an action against defendant New York State Thruway Authority to permanently enjoin the Authority from removing the company's signs along the roadways under authority claimed pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 361-a(2). The Authority filed a cross-motion for an order dismissing the company's complaint, contending that the court did not have jurisdiction over the subject matter of the action.


OVERVIEW: The company obtained an order requiring the Authority to show cause to preclude the court from enjoining the Authority pendent lite from removing the company's signs under § 361-a(2). The show cause order granted the temporary restraint sought. On a cross-motion, the Authority sought an order dismissing the company's complaint, based on the Authority's contention that the court lacked jurisdiction over the subject matter. The court determined that there was no statutory authority for the maintenance of the company's action against the Authority based on the governmental immunity legislatively provided for the Authority. The court criticized the Authority's conduct and granted its motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court denied the company's motion for an injunction pendente lite and granted the Authority's cross-motion to dismiss the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- jurisdiction -- Thruway Authority -- Supreme Court lacked jurisdiction of equity action against Thruway Authority.

The Supreme Court lacked jurisdiction of an action in equity to restrain the Thruway Authority from tearing down billboards containing advertising which had been erected within 660 feet of the nearest edge of the pavement of the Thruway in violation of section 361-a of the Public Authorities Law. While the Legislature waived the Thruway's immunity for torts or breaches of contract, it did not permit maintenance of an action in equity against the Thruway Authority. The complaint was dismissed.

 

2320 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reshes


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


39 Misc. 2d 723; 242 N.Y.S.2d 416; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1806



July 12, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] As to all of the other exhibits, the motion is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the trial court (New York), defendants filed motions to suppress the use of certain evidence seized from their stores in their arrests for pandering obscene material.


OVERVIEW: The police were shown a list of book titles and were directed to 20 bookstores in Times Square. The officers visited the shops assigned to them, buying certain books and photographs. The police examined their purchases and arrested defendants. The police then searched the premises and seized other materials. Defendants were charged with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 1141. Defendants filed motions to suppress the evidence. The court denied the motions with respect to all of the purchased exhibits, but granted the motion as to all of the other exhibits. The court held that there were no violations of defendants' rights under U.S. Const. amends. I or IV. The court found that the voluntary sale of alleged obscene material to a person, who turned out to be a police officer, for which sale the seller was arrested and prosecuted, did not constitute suppression of freedom of speech or thought, any more than it constituted denial of due process. The court held that the act of offering for sale, or sale, of obscene material to a police officer, constituted the commission of a misdemeanor in his presence, for which an arrest may have been made without a warrant under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 177.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motions to suppress with respect to all of the purchased exhibits, but granted the motion as to all of the other exhibits.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- purchase of photographs and books openly displayed in public book shops was not unlawful search or seizure -- act of selling obscene material to police officer was commission of misdemeanor for which arrests without warrant were proper -- no suppression of speech or thought was involved in voluntary sale -- prior planning and co-ordinated execution of purchase by police officers not constitutionally proscribed -- motion to suppress evidence denied.

1. The purchase of photographs and books, openly displayed in public book shops, then open for business, by police did not constitute a search of any kind and such purchase did not constitute an illegal search and seizure.

2. The act of selling obscene material to a police officer constituted the commission of a misdemeanor in his presence for which an arrest was properly made without a warrant. No violation of defendants' constitutional rights under the Fourth Amendment occurred.

3. Nor was there any violation of defendants' rights under the First or Fourteenth Amendments. The voluntary sale of alleged obscene material to a [***2] person who turned out to be a police officer, for which sale the seller was arrested and prosecuted did not constitute suppression of speech or thought or denial of due process.

4. The prior planning and co-ordinated execution by the police of the purchases of the photographs and books was not constitutionally proscribed.

5. A motion to suppress the evidence was denied.

 

2321 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tourists International, S. A.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 99; 242 N.Y.S.2d 756; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1815



July 10, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions for dismissal of the complaint and for summary judgment are granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant shipping companies filed motions to dismiss a complaint brought by the state, which alleged that they violated several provisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law. Plaintiff shipping companies filed motions for judgment on the pleading or, in the alternative, summary judgment in the declaratory judgment action against defendants, chairman and commissioner of the state liquor authority. The motions were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: In two separate actions which arose from alleged violations of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, the state alleged that defendants violated the law by engaging in interstate and international alcohol shipping activities, and advertising and solicitation of liquor sales and purchases. Plaintiffs sought declaratory judgment against the chairman and the commissioner, who determined that plaintiffs could not deliver alcohol to state residents that was purchased by those residents while they were outside of the United States. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. Plaintiffs filed motions for judgment on the pleadings or, in the alternative, for summary judgment. The actions were consolidated. The court granted the motions because the activities of defendants and plaintiffs did not violate any of the provisions of the law. The court held that the purpose of the law was to regulate the manufacture, sale, and distribution of alcoholic beverages within the state, and not to regulate activities outside of the state. Further, the court held that plaintiffs' activities were specifically allowed by N.Y. Alco. Bev. Cont. Law § 116(c).


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint that was filed against it by the state. The court granted plaintiffs' motions for summary judgment in its declaratory judgment action against the commissioner and the chairman.


HEADNOTES

Intoxicating liquors -- purchase of liquor in foreign country by resident -- Alcoholic Beverage Control Law did not prohibit purchase abroad by foreign travelers of alcoholic beverages "duty free" with delivery of liquor to home of purchaser by licensed trucking agency which picked it up at shipside.

1. Section 100 (subd. 1) of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law prohibited the sale of liquor within the State by any person unless licensed. Section 102 prohibited the advertising of solicitations for an order for alcoholic beverages except by licensed persons, prohibited the shipment of alcoholic beverages into the State except to licensed consignees and prohibited carriers from bringing into the State alcoholic beverages unless consigned to licensees. Defendants in the first action, unlicensed persons, sent advertisements into the State whereby travelers outside the United States could bring into the State "duty free" liquor and plaintiffs in the second action were carriers licensed to transport liquor within the State who delivered to New York residents alcoholic beverages which they purchased [***2] outside the State and shipped such alcoholic beverages to themselves as consignees. The activities of defendants in the first action and plaintiffs in the second action did not violate the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law. The legislative purpose of the statute was to regulate the manufacture, sale and distribution of alcoholic beverages within the State. Here, the parties to the contract of sale demonstrated their intention that title pass outside the State, where the order was placed and accepted, the payment was received, and the liquor purchased was appropriated to the contract. The prohibition against advertising and soliciting orders applied only with respect to alcoholic beverages to be sold within the State. Here, not only were the sales consummated outside the State, but the orders were placed outside the State as well. By failing to include in the sections a prohibition against sales made outside the State by a purchaser outside the State, the Legislature indicated its intent that the sections did not apply.

2. Section 116 (cl. [c]) of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law provided that alcoholic beverages might be delivered from a steamship to a purchaser for consumption [***3] by a trucking agency licensed under such law. The deliveries by plaintiffs in the second action were permitted by such section and the right to make them was not taken away by section 102.

 

2322 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kew Gardens Sanitarium, Inc. v. Trussell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


39 Misc. 2d 742; 241 N.Y.S.2d 985; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1829



July 3, 1963 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In view of the foregoing, the petition is granted, respondent's determination is annulled and respondent is directed to issue an annual license for the operation of the Hospital.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sanitarium filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 action against respondent, Commissioner of Hospitals of the City of New York (commissioner), seeking reversal of the commissioner's decision to refuse to renew the sanitarium's annual license to conduct a private proprietary hospital, and to compel the commissioner to issue such a license.


OVERVIEW: The sanitarium alleged that it was in compliance with § 35(b) of the Social Welfare Law and that the sole reason for the commissioner's refusal to renew its license was the failure of the sanitarium to amend its leases. There was a lease between the sanitarium and the landlord and a sublease of space from the sanitarium to two radiologists, who paid the sanitarium 21.2 percent of their gross receipts. The sanitarium argued that the refusal was arbitrary and capricious, contrary to law and unconstitutional. The court granted the sanitarium's petition and ordered the commissioner to issue an annual license for the operation of the sanitarium. The court found that the sanitarium did not practice medicine. It merely rented space to the radiologists who provided, and billed for, their medical care. The sanitarium only charged for board, lodging, non-medical care, and nursing. Such being the case, there was no basis for holding the leases invalid because neither the landlord nor the sanitarium were unlawfully participating in the practice of medicine. Additionally, N.Y. Educ. Law § 6514(2) allowed the radiologists to pay a rental amount not to exceed 33.3 percent for use of facilities.


OUTCOME: The court granted the sanitarium's petition, annulled the commissioner's determination, and directed the commissioner to issue the sanitarium an annual license.


HEADNOTES

Hospitals and asylums -- lawfulness, as rent, of percentage of gross receipts -- denial of renewal of annual license to operate private proprietary hospital on ground that hospital's lease, and sublease of radiology department were based on percentage of gross receipts was annulled -- petitioner, operating hospital prior to 1956 enactment of section 35-b of Social Welfare Law, providing that only licensed physicians might operate hospital for profit, fell within exception in said section entitling it to continue to operate -- hospital, by supplying facilities to patients of doctors, was not practicing medicine -- landlord did not operate hospital -- payment of percentage of gross receipts as rent was not unlawful and was proper.

1. The denial of the renewal of petitioner's annual license to operate a private proprietary hospital by the Commissioner of Hospitals of the City of New York, on the ground that the hospital's lease of the premises and the sublease of space in the hospital for the operation [***2] of the radiology department were based on percentages of gross receipts, was annulled.

2. Section 35-b of the Social Welfare Law, added in 1956, provided that only duly licensed physicians might operate hospitals for profit, except licensed hospitals in operation on the date the section took effect. Since petitioner was operating its hospital before the section took effect, it was entitled to continue to be licensed.

3. The hospital, by supplying facilities to patients of doctors and surgeons who alone rendered medical and surgical care, was not practicing medicine. The lease was therefore not invalid on the ground asserted by respondent Commissioner that the hospital was unlawfully participating in the practice of medicine.

4. The landlord did not operate the hospital. The lease between the sanitarium and landlord was executed at arm's length. The percentage rental provisions did not place landlord in any different position so far as operation of the hospital was concerned than would fixed rental provisions.

5. Subdivision 2 of section 6514 of the Education Law provided for the punishment of a practitioner of medicine for offenses stated therein. Paragraph (f) dealt with [***3] fee splitting but excepted payment up to 33 1/3% of any fee "received for x-ray examination * * * to any hospital furnishing facilities". Since the operators of the radiology department of the hospital were obligated to pay 21.2% of their gross receipts, their sublease with the operator was neither unlawful nor unethical. The inclusion of the rent from the operation of the radiology department in landlord's percentage was proper and, in any event, neither the operator nor the landlord was engaged in the practice of medicine.

 

2323 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. Baumgartner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, New York County


40 Misc. 2d 221; 242 N.Y.S.2d 910; 1963 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1850



June 28, 1963 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tattoo parlor operators filed an action for injunctive relief against defendants, a municipality's administrative health agency and its commissioner, asserting that New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 181.15 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The agency adopted New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 181.15, which made it unlawful for any person to tattoo a human being, with the exception that tattooing could be performed for medical purposes. Thereafter, the operators filed an action against the agency and its commissioner, asserting that the law was unconstitutional. The court found that the law was designed to insure sanitary and sterile procedures for tattooing establishments.
